### Create TanStack Start Project

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/tanstack-start

Initialize a new TanStack Start project using Create Start App. This command creates a new project directory and installs all necessary dependencies for a TanStack Start application.

```bash
npx create-start-app@latest my-project
cd my-project
```

### Create Symfony Project with CLI

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/symfony

Initialize a new Symfony web project using the Symfony Installer. This command creates a new project directory and navigates into it for subsequent setup steps.

```bash
symfony new --webapp my-project
cd my-project
```

---

### Start the Meteor development server

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/meteor

Executes the `npm run start` command to initiate the Meteor development server and build process. This command compiles your application, watches for changes, and serves it locally for development.

```Terminal
npm run start
```

---

### Create a new Nuxt.js project using npm

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/nuxt

This command initializes a fresh Nuxt.js project named 'my-project' in the current directory. It then navigates into the newly created project folder, preparing the environment for further setup and dependency installation.

```Terminal
npm create nuxt my-project
cd my-project
```

---

### Start Gatsby Development Server

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/gatsby

Run the Gatsby development server to build and serve the project. This command watches for file changes and rebuilds the site automatically.

```bash
gatsby develop
```

---

### Start Laravel Mix build process

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/laravel/mix

Run the npm watch command to start the build process. This command watches for changes in your files and automatically recompiles your CSS and JavaScript.

```bash
npm run watch
```

---

### Include compiled Tailwind CSS in HTML and use utility classes

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/tailwind-cli

This HTML snippet demonstrates how to link the compiled `output.css` file in your document's `<head>` section. It also shows a basic example of using Tailwind's utility classes (e.g., `text-3xl`, `font-bold`, `underline`) to style an `<h1>` element.

```html
<!doctype html>
<html>
  <head>
    <meta charset="UTF-8" />
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0" />
    <link href="./output.css" rel="stylesheet" />
  </head>
  <body>
    <h1 class="text-3xl font-bold underline">Hello world!</h1>
  </body>
</html>
```

---

### Install Tailwind CSS and CLI via npm

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/tailwind-cli

This command installs the core Tailwind CSS library and the Tailwind CLI tool as development dependencies in your project. It's the first step to get the necessary packages for building your CSS.

```Terminal
npm install tailwindcss @tailwindcss/cli
```

---

### Start Rails Development Server

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/ruby-on-rails

Run the development server with the build process using the ./bin/dev command. This starts both the Rails server and the Tailwind CSS build watcher to compile styles as you develop.

```bash
./bin/dev
```

---

### Start Parcel development server and build process

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/parcel

This command initiates the Parcel build process for the specified entry point (`src/index.html`). Parcel will compile all linked assets, including HTML, CSS, and JavaScript, and typically starts a development server with live reloading capabilities for efficient development.

```Terminal
npx parcel src/index.html
```

---

### Start Development Server

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/adonisjs

Run the npm dev script to start the AdonisJS development server with Vite. This enables hot module replacement and automatic CSS compilation with Tailwind CSS.

```bash
npm run dev
```

---

### Start Phoenix server with Tailwind CSS build

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/phoenix

Run the `mix phx.server` command to start your Phoenix development server. This will also trigger the configured Tailwind CSS build process, compiling your styles and making them available in your application.

```bash
mix phx.server
```

---

### Run Tailwind CLI to build CSS with watch mode

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/tailwind-cli

Execute the Tailwind CLI to scan your source files for utility classes, process your input CSS, and generate the final output CSS file. The `--watch` flag keeps the process running, automatically recompiling your CSS whenever changes are detected in your source files.

```Terminal
npx @tailwindcss/cli -i ./src/input.css -o ./src/output.css --watch
```

---

### Start Angular Development Server

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/angular

Run the Angular development server to compile the project and enable hot module reloading. The server watches for file changes and automatically rebuilds the application.

```bash
ng serve
```

---

### Snap Start Alignment with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/scroll-snap-align

Demonstrates using the snap-start utility to snap an element to its start position when scrolled inside a snap container. This example shows a horizontally scrollable grid of images where each image snaps to the start of the viewport.

```html
<div class="snap-x ...">
  <div class="snap-start ...">
    <img src="/img/vacation-01.jpg" />
  </div>
  <div class="snap-start ...">
    <img src="/img/vacation-02.jpg" />
  </div>
  <div class="snap-start ...">
    <img src="/img/vacation-03.jpg" />
  </div>
  <div class="snap-start ...">
    <img src="/img/vacation-04.jpg" />
  </div>
  <div class="snap-start ...">
    <img src="/img/vacation-05.jpg" />
  </div>
  <div class="snap-start ...">
    <img src="/img/vacation-06.jpg" />
  </div>
</div>
```

---

### Applying styles to elements at their starting state with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example illustrates the `starting` variant in Tailwind CSS, which allows setting the initial appearance of an element when it is first rendered or transitions from `display: none` to visible. It's particularly useful for defining entry animations or initial states.

```html
<div>
  <button popovertarget="my-popover">Check for updates</button>
  <div popover id="my-popover" class="opacity-0 starting:open:opacity-0 ...">
    <!-- ... -->
  </div>
</div>
```

### Link CSS File in Root Route

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/tanstack-start

Import the compiled CSS file in your root route component using the ?url query parameter. This ensures the stylesheet is loaded globally for all pages in your TanStack Start application.

```typescript
// other imports...
import appCss from "../styles.css?url";

export const Route = createRootRoute({
  head: () => ({
    meta: [
      // your meta tags and site config
    ],
    links: [{ rel: "stylesheet", href: appCss }],
    // other head config
  }),
  component: RootComponent,
});
```

### Configure Vite Plugin for Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/tanstack-start

Add the @tailwindcss/vite plugin to your Vite configuration file. This plugin must be placed before other plugins in the plugins array to ensure proper CSS processing and integration with TanStack Start.

```typescript
import { tanstackStart } from "@tanstack/react-start/plugin/vite";
import { defineConfig } from "vite";
import tsConfigPaths from "vite-tsconfig-paths";
import tailwindcss from "@tailwindcss/vite";

export default defineConfig({
  plugins: [tailwindcss(), tanstackStart(), tsConfigPaths()],
});
```

---

### flex-basis Responsive Design Example - HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/flex-basis

Demonstrates responsive flex-basis utilities using breakpoint variants. The example shows how to apply different basis values at different screen sizes using the md: prefix for medium screens and above.

```html
<div class="flex flex-row">
  <div class="basis-1/4 md:basis-1/3">01</div>
  <div class="basis-1/4 md:basis-1/3">02</div>
  <div class="basis-1/2 md:basis-1/3">03</div>
</div>
```

### HTML Template with Tailwind CSS Utilities

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation

Basic HTML template demonstrating Tailwind CSS utility classes. Includes the compiled CSS link in the head and uses Tailwind utility classes like text-3xl, font-bold, and underline to style content.

```html
<!doctype html>
<html>
  <head>
    <meta charset="UTF-8" />
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0" />
    <link href="/src/style.css" rel="stylesheet" />
  </head>
  <body>
    <h1 class="text-3xl font-bold underline">Hello world!</h1>
  </body>
</html>
```

### Grid row start and end positioning in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/grid-row

Shows how to use row-start-<number> and row-end-<number> utilities to position elements at specific grid lines. The example demonstrates starting and ending elements at different grid lines, with optional row-span utilities for additional control.

```html
<div class="grid grid-flow-col grid-rows-3 gap-4">
  <div class="row-span-2 row-start-2 ...">01</div>
  <div class="row-span-2 row-end-3 ...">02</div>
  <div class="row-start-1 row-end-4 ...">03</div>
</div>
```

### Apply background-origin utilities in HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/background-origin

This example demonstrates how to use the `bg-origin-border`, `bg-origin-padding`, and `bg-origin-content` utilities to control where an element's background image is rendered. Each class sets the `background-origin` CSS property to `border-box`, `padding-box`, or `content-box` respectively, affecting the background's starting point.

```html
<div
  class="border-4 bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)] bg-origin-border p-3 ..."
></div>
<div
  class="border-4 bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)] bg-origin-padding p-3 ..."
></div>
<div
  class="border-4 bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)] bg-origin-content p-3 ..."
></div>
```

### Configure Tailwind CSS Vite plugin in vite.config.ts

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/index

This configuration snippet adds the `@tailwindcss/vite` plugin to the Vite build process. By importing `defineConfig` from `vite` and `tailwindcss` from `@tailwindcss/vite`, it enables Tailwind CSS to process class names found in project files and generate the corresponding CSS. This setup is crucial for Tailwind's JIT (Just-In-Time) compilation.

```TypeScript
import { defineConfig } from 'vite'
import tailwindcss from '@tailwindcss/vite'

export default defineConfig({
  plugins: [
    tailwindcss(),
  ],
})
```

### Configure Tailwind CSS plugin in Phoenix

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/phoenix

Configure the Tailwind plugin in `config/config.exs` to specify the desired Tailwind CSS version and define the input/output paths for your stylesheets. This setup directs where Tailwind should read your source CSS and where to output the compiled CSS.

```elixir
config :tailwind,
  version: "4.1.10",
  myproject: [
    args: ~w(
      --input=assets/css/app.css
      --output=priv/static/assets/app.css
    ),
    cd: Path.expand("..", __DIR__)
  ]
```

### Basic transition-behavior HTML Example

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/transition-behavior

Demonstrates the use of transition-discrete utility to handle transitions on elements that change from hidden to block state. Shows two examples: one with transition-normal (immediate hide) and one with transition-discrete (fade out effect). Uses Tailwind CSS classes with peer selectors and checkbox interactions.

```html
<label class="peer ...">
  <input type="checkbox" checked />
</label>
<button
  class="hidden transition-all not-peer-has-checked:opacity-0 peer-has-checked:block ..."
>
  I hide
</button>
<label class="peer ...">
  <input type="checkbox" checked />
</label>
<button
  class="hidden transition-all transition-discrete not-peer-has-checked:opacity-0 peer-has-checked:block ..."
>
  I fade out
</button>
```

---

### Tailwind CSS `start` Utilities for Inline Start Placement

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/top-right-bottom-left

These utilities control the `inset-inline-start` CSS property, setting the logical start position of an element within its inline direction. They offer options for numeric, fractional, pixel, full percentage, auto, custom property, and arbitrary values, including negative variants.

```css
/* start-<number> */
inset-inline-start: calc(var(--spacing) * <number>);
```

```css
/* -start-<number> */
inset-inline-start: calc(var(--spacing) * -<number>);
```

```css
/* start-<fraction> */
inset-inline-start: calc(<fraction> * 100%);
```

```css
/* -start-<fraction> */
inset-inline-start: calc(<fraction> * -100%);
```

```css
/* start-px */
inset-inline-start: 1px;
```

```css
/* -start-px */
inset-inline-start: -1px;
```

```css
/* start-full */
inset-inline-start: 100%;
```

```css
/* -start-full */
inset-inline-start: -100%;
```

```css
/* start-auto */
inset-inline-start: auto;
```

```css
/* start-(<custom-property>) */
inset-inline-start: var(<custom-property>);
```

```css
/* start-[<value>] */
inset-inline-start: <value>;
```

### perspective-origin Basic HTML Example with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/perspective-origin

Demonstrates using perspective-origin utilities to control the vanishing point location in 3D space. Shows two examples with perspective-origin-top-left and perspective-origin-bottom-right applied to containers with 3D transformed child elements.

```html
<div class="size-20 perspective-near perspective-origin-top-left ...">
  <div class="translate-z-12 rotate-x-0 bg-sky-300/75 ...">1</div>
  <div class="-translate-z-12 rotate-y-18 bg-sky-300/75 ...">2</div>
  <div class="translate-x-12 rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">3</div>
  <div class="-translate-x-12 -rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">4</div>
  <div class="-translate-y-12 rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">5</div>
  <div class="translate-y-12 -rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">6</div>
</div>
<div class="size-20 perspective-near perspective-origin-bottom-right …">
  <div class="translate-z-12 rotate-x-0 bg-sky-300/75 ...">1</div>
  <div class="-translate-z-12 rotate-y-18 bg-sky-300/75 ...">2</div>
  <div class="translate-x-12 rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">3</div>
  <div class="-translate-x-12 -rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">4</div>
  <div class="-translate-y-12 rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">5</div>
  <div class="translate-y-12 -rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">6</div>
</div>
```

### Use Tailwind CSS utility classes in HTML

    <link href="/dist/styles.css" rel="stylesheet" />
  </head>

  </body>
</html>

This shows the final integration of Tailwind CSS into an application's UI.

};

### Configure Tailwind CSS Vite plugin in vite.config.ts

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/laravel/vite

```typescript
import { defineConfig } from "vite";
import tailwindcss from "@tailwindcss/vite";

export default defineConfig({
  plugins: [
    tailwindcss(),
    // …
  ],
});
```

### Container Query Range Targeting

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

Combine regular container query variants with max-width variants to target a specific container size range. This example applies flex-col only when container is between sm and md sizes.

```html
<div class="@container">
  <div class="flex flex-row @sm:@max-md:flex-col">
    <!-- ... -->
  </div>
</div>
```

This example demonstrates how to directly apply Tailwind's utility classes within the `<template>` section of a Vue component, specifically in `app.vue`. It shows styling an `<h1>` element with `text-3xl`, `font-bold`, and `underline` classes, illustrating the direct application of Tailwind for rapid UI development.

```html
<div class="w-40 ...">
  <div class="min-w-lg ...">min-w-lg</div>
  <div class="min-w-md ...">min-w-md</div>
  <div class="min-w-sm ...">min-w-sm</div>
  <div class="min-w-xs ...">min-w-xs</div>

  <img class="float-left ..." src="/img/green-mountains.jpg" />

### Configure Tailwind CSS Vite Plugin

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/qwik

Add the @tailwindcss/vite plugin to the Vite configuration file. This enables Tailwind CSS processing during the build process alongside other Qwik plugins.

```typescript
import { defineConfig } from "vite";
import { qwikVite } from "@builder.io/qwik/optimizer";
import { qwikCity } from "@builder.io/qwik-city/vite";
// …
import tailwindcss from "@tailwindcss/vite";

export default defineConfig(({ command, mode }): UserConfig => {
  return {
    plugins: [tailwindcss(), qwikCity(), qwikVite(), tsconfigPaths()],
    // …
  };
});
```

### Applying custom flex-shrink values in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/flex-shrink

This example shows how to use the arbitrary value syntax `shrink-[<value>]` in Tailwind CSS to set a custom flex shrink factor. It demonstrates applying a dynamic calculation for the shrink value, allowing for highly specific control.

```html
<div class="shrink-[calc(100vw-var(--sidebar))] ..."><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Responsive order utility with breakpoint variants

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/order

Prefix an order utility with a breakpoint variant like md: to only apply the utility at medium screen sizes and above. This example applies order-first on mobile and order-last on medium screens and larger.

```html
<div class="order-first md:order-last ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Use Tailwind CSS in AdonisJS Edge Template

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/adonisjs

Include the compiled CSS file in the HTML head using @vite helper and apply Tailwind utility classes to HTML elements. This example demonstrates basic Tailwind styling with text size, font weight, and text decoration utilities.

```html
<!doctype html>
<html>
  <head>
    <meta charset="utf-8" />
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0" />
    @vite(['resources/css/app.css', 'resources/js/app.js'])
  </head>
  <body>
    <h1 class="text-3xl font-bold underline">Hello world!</h1>
  </body>
</html>
```

### perspective-origin Responsive Design with Tailwind CSS

---

### Remove Default Breakpoints

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

Reset individual or all default breakpoints using the initial keyword in the @theme block. This example removes the 2xl breakpoint, or alternatively resets all breakpoints and defines custom ones from scratch.

```css
@import "tailwindcss";
@theme {
  --breakpoint-2xl: initial;
}
```

```css
@import "tailwindcss";
@theme {
  --breakpoint-*: initial;
  --breakpoint-tablet: 40rem;
  --breakpoint-laptop: 64rem;
  --breakpoint-desktop: 80rem;
}
```

---

### Import CSS in SvelteKit Layout Component

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/sveltekit

Create a +layout.svelte file in src/routes and import the app.css file. This ensures Tailwind CSS styles are available throughout the entire SvelteKit application.

```svelte
<script>
  let { children } = $props();
  import "../app.css";
</script>

{@render children()}
```

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/laravel/mix

```html
<!doctype html>

    <meta charset="utf-8" />

    <link href="{{ asset('css/app.css') }}" rel="stylesheet" />

  </body>
</html>

### Apply content-start to align rows to the start of the cross axis in HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/align-content

This HTML snippet demonstrates how to use the `content-start` utility class in Tailwind CSS to align rows to the beginning of the cross axis within a grid container. It sets the container height, defines a 3-column grid, and applies `content-start` to pack the content rows against the start.

```html
<div class="grid h-56 grid-cols-3 content-start gap-4 ...">
  <div>01</div>
  <div>02</div>
  <div>03</div>
  <div>04</div>
  <div>05</div>
</div>
```

### Implement Radial Gradients with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/background-image

Shows how to apply radial gradients using Tailwind CSS utilities. This includes basic radial gradients and examples with custom positioning and multiple color stops, demonstrating flexibility in gradient design.

```html
<div
  class="size-18 rounded-full bg-radial from-pink-400 from-40% to-fuchsia-700"
></div>
<div
  class="size-18 rounded-full bg-radial-[at_50%_75%] from-sky-200 via-blue-400 to-indigo-900 to-90%"
></div>
<div
  class="size-18 rounded-full bg-radial-[at_25%_25%] from-white to-zinc-900 to-75%"
></div>
```

  <div>06</div>

### Understand Tailwind CSS Gradient Variant Overrides (v3 HTML)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Illustrates how Tailwind CSS v3 would 'reset' an entire gradient when a variant overrode only part of it. In this example, `dark:from-blue-500` would cause the `to-*` color to become transparent in dark mode.

```html
<div class="bg-gradient-to-r from-red-500 to-yellow-400 dark:from-blue-500">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Configure PostCSS Plugins

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/gatsby

Create a postcss.config.js file at the project root and register the @tailwindcss/postcss plugin. This enables PostCSS to process Tailwind CSS directives.

```javascript
module.exports = {
  plugins: {
    "@tailwindcss/postcss": {},
  },
};
```

### Translate elements using Tailwind CSS percentage values

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/translate

This example illustrates 2D translations using Tailwind CSS `translate-<fraction>` utilities, where translation distances are expressed as percentages of the element's size. It includes examples of both positive and negative percentage-based translations.

```html
<img class="-translate-1/4 ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" /><img
  class="translate-1/6 ..."
  src="/img/mountains.jpg"
/><img class="translate-1/2 ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
```

---

### Update Transition Properties for Individual Transforms - HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Include individual transform properties (rotate, scale, translate) instead of the generic transform property in custom transition lists. For example, use transition-[opacity,scale] instead of transition-[opacity,transform] when transitioning scale utilities.

```html
<button class="transition-[opacity,scale] hover:scale-150"></button>
```

### Apply backface-visibility utilities in HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/backface-visibility

This example demonstrates how to use `backface-hidden` and `backface-visible` Tailwind CSS utilities on elements within a 3D transformed context. It shows two sets of elements, one with hidden backfaces and one with visible backfaces, to illustrate the effect when elements are rotated away from the viewer.

```html
<div class="size-20 ...">
  <div class="translate-z-12 rotate-x-0 bg-sky-300/75 backface-hidden ...">
    1
  </div>
  <div class="-translate-z-12 rotate-y-18 bg-sky-300/75 backface-hidden ...">
    2
  </div>
  <div class="translate-x-12 rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 backface-hidden ...">
    3
  </div>
  <div class="-translate-x-12 -rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 backface-hidden ...">
    4
  </div>
  <div class="-translate-y-12 rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 backface-hidden ...">
    5
  </div>
  <div class="translate-y-12 -rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 backface-hidden ...">
    6
  </div>
</div>
<div class="size-20 ...">
  <div class="translate-z-12 rotate-x-0 bg-sky-300/75 backface-visible ...">
    1
  </div>
  <div class="-translate-z-12 rotate-y-18 bg-sky-300/75 backface-visible ...">
    2
  </div>
  <div class="translate-x-12 rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 backface-visible ...">
    3
  </div>
  <div class="-translate-x-12 -rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 backface-visible ...">
    4
  </div>
  <div class="-translate-y-12 rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 backface-visible ...">
    5
  </div>
  <div class="translate-y-12 -rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 backface-visible ...">
    6
  </div>
</div>
```

### Generate Conic Gradients with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/background-image

Demonstrates how to create conic gradients using Tailwind CSS utilities. Examples cover basic conic gradients, those with specific angles, and variations in color stop configurations for diverse visual effects.

```html

  class="size-24 rounded-full bg-conic from-blue-600 to-sky-400 to-50%"
></div>

### Add Play CDN Script to HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/play-cdn

Add the Tailwind CSS Play CDN script tag to the HTML head element to enable Tailwind utility classes without any build step. This method is designed for development purposes only and not recommended for production use. Allows immediate styling of content using Tailwind's utility classes.

```html
<!doctype html>
<html>
  <head>
    <meta charset="UTF-8" />
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0" />
    <script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/@tailwindcss/browser@4"></script>
  </head>
  <body>
    <h1 class="text-3xl font-bold underline">Hello world!</h1>
  </body>
</html>
```

### Update Tailwind CSS Shadow, Radius, and Blur Utilities (v3 to v4)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Explains the renaming of default shadow, radius, and blur scales in Tailwind CSS v4. The 'bare' versions still work, but utilities like `_<utility>_-sm` will look different unless updated to their respective `_<utility>_-xs` versions. This snippet shows examples of v3 and v4 utility usage.

```html
<input class="shadow-sm" /><input class="shadow-xs" /><input
  class="shadow"
/><input class="shadow-sm" />
```

### flex-none Utility Example

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/flex

Shows how to use flex-none to prevent flex items from growing or shrinking. Items 01 and 02 maintain their fixed widths regardless of container size, while item 03 with flex-1 takes remaining space.

```html
<div class="flex ...">
  <div class="w-14 flex-none ...">01</div>
  <div class="w-32 flex-none ...">02</div>
  <div class="flex-1 ...">03</div>
</div>
```

This example demonstrates using the `opacity-(<custom-property>)` syntax to apply opacity based on a CSS custom property, like `--my-opacity`. This is a shorthand for `opacity-[var(<custom-property>)]`.

```html
<button class="opacity-(--my-opacity) ..."><!-- ... --></button>
```

---

### Configure Custom Tailwind CSS Theme with Play CDN

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/play-cdn

Use the Play CDN with custom CSS by adding a style tag with type="text/tailwindcss" to define theme variables and custom styles. This approach supports all of Tailwind's CSS features including theme customization, allowing developers to extend the default color palette and other design tokens directly in HTML.

```html
<!doctype html>
<html>
  <head>
    <meta charset="UTF-8" />
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0" />
    <script src="https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/npm/@tailwindcss/browser@4"></script>
    <style type="text/tailwindcss">
      @theme {
        --color-clifford: #da373d;
      }
    </style>
  </head>
  <body>
    <h1 class="text-3xl font-bold underline text-clifford">Hello world!</h1>
  </body>
</html>
```

---

### Apply Hardware Acceleration with Tailwind CSS `transform-gpu`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/transform

This example demonstrates how to force hardware acceleration for element transformations using the `transform-gpu` utility in Tailwind CSS. This can improve performance for transitions by offloading rendering to the GPU. The `transform-cpu` utility can be used to revert this behavior.

```html
<div class="scale-150 transform-gpu"><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Adjust Tailwind CSS Outline Utility Default Width (v3 to v4)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Details the change in Tailwind CSS v4 where the `outline` utility now defaults to `outline-width: 1px` for consistency with border and ring utilities. Furthermore, `outline-<number>` utilities now default `outline-style` to `solid`. This example shows the implicit solid style.

```html
<input class="outline outline-2" /><input class="outline-2" />
```

### Apply Basic Grayscale Filters with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/filter-grayscale

Demonstrates applying different grayscale levels to images using Tailwind CSS utility classes. Examples include `grayscale-0` (no grayscale), `grayscale-25` (25% grayscale), `grayscale-50` (50% grayscale), and `grayscale` (100% grayscale).

```html
<img class="grayscale-0 ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" /><img
  class="grayscale-25 ..."
  src="/img/mountains.jpg"
/><img class="grayscale-50 ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" /><img
  class="grayscale ..."
  src="/img/mountains.jpg"
/>
```

It applies `bg-blend-lighten` by default and dynamically switches to `md:bg-blend-darken` for medium screen sizes and above, showcasing how to adapt blending modes based on viewport dimensions.

### place-items-start - Align grid items to start

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/place-items

Positions grid items at the start of their grid areas on both horizontal and vertical axes. Use this class on a grid container to align all child items to the top-left corner of their respective grid cells.

```html
<div class="grid grid-cols-3 place-items-start gap-4 ...">
  <div>01</div>
  <div>02</div>
  <div>03</div>
  <div>04</div>
  <div>05</div>
  <div>06</div>
</div>

This example illustrates how to apply `mix-blend-mode` utilities conditionally based on screen size using responsive prefixes like `md:`. The `mix-blend-multiply` class is applied by default, and `md:mix-blend-overlay` overrides it for medium screens and above.

---

### Configure Tailwind CSS Vite Plugin

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/sveltekit

Add the @tailwindcss/vite plugin to the Vite configuration file. This enables Tailwind CSS processing during development and production builds alongside the SvelteKit plugin.

```typescript
import { sveltekit } from "@sveltejs/kit/vite";
import { defineConfig } from "vite";
import tailwindcss from "@tailwindcss/vite";

export default defineConfig({
  plugins: [tailwindcss(), sveltekit()],
});
```

### Pointer events comparison example

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/pointer-events

Demonstrates the difference between pointer-events-auto and pointer-events-none on overlaid SVG icons above an input field. The pointer-events-auto version allows interactions on the icon, while pointer-events-none makes the icon transparent to pointer events, allowing clicks to reach the input beneath.

```html
<div class="relative ...">
  <div class="pointer-events-auto absolute ...">
    <svg class="absolute h-5 w-5 text-gray-400">
      <!-- ... -->
    </svg>
  </div>
  <input type="text" placeholder="Search" class="..." />
</div>
<div class="relative ...">
  <div class="pointer-events-none absolute ...">
    <svg class="absolute h-5 w-5 text-gray-400">
      <!-- ... -->
    </svg>
  </div>
  <input type="text" placeholder="Search" class="..." />
</div>
```

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/flex-basis

Shows two methods for using custom values: the basis-[<value>] syntax for arbitrary CSS values and the basis-(<custom-property>) syntax for CSS variables. Both approaches allow flexibility beyond predefined utilities.

```html
<div class="basis-[30vw] ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>

<div class="basis-(--my-basis) ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Isolate blending context with Tailwind CSS

```html

  <div class="bg-yellow-500 mix-blend-multiply ..."></div>
  <div class="bg-green-500 mix-blend-multiply ..."></div>
</div>
<div class="flex justify-center -space-x-14">
  <div class="bg-yellow-500 mix-blend-multiply ..."></div>
  <div class="bg-green-500 mix-blend-multiply ..."></div>
</div>

### Apply Custom Minimum Width with Tailwind CSS Variables Shorthand

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/min-width

<div class="min-w-(--my-min-width) ..."><!-- ... --></div>

### Set Percentage-Based Widths with Tailwind CSS w-<fraction> Utilities

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/width

This example illustrates how to apply percentage-based widths to elements using Tailwind CSS `w-full` or `w-<fraction>` utilities. These classes are ideal for creating responsive layouts where elements occupy a specific proportion of their parent container's width.

```html
<div class="flex ...">
  <div class="w-1/2 ...">w-1/2</div>
  <div class="w-1/2 ...">w-1/2</div>
</div>
<div class="flex ...">
  <div class="w-2/5 ...">w-2/5</div>
  <div class="w-3/5 ...">w-3/5</div>
</div>
<div class="flex ...">
  <div class="w-1/3 ...">w-1/3</div>
  <div class="w-2/3 ...">w-2/3</div>
</div>
<div class="flex ...">
  <div class="w-1/4 ...">w-1/4</div>
  <div class="w-3/4 ...">w-3/4</div>
</div>
<div class="flex ...">
  <div class="w-1/5 ...">w-1/5</div>
  <div class="w-4/5 ...">w-4/5</div>
</div>
<div class="flex ...">
  <div class="w-1/6 ...">w-1/6</div>
  <div class="w-5/6 ...">w-5/6</div>
</div>
<div class="w-full ...">w-full</div>
```

### Apply Tailwind CSS touch-action utilities for basic touch control

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/touch-action

This example demonstrates how to use various Tailwind CSS `touch-action` utilities such as `touch-auto`, `touch-none`, `touch-pan-x`, and `touch-pan-y` to control scrolling and zooming behavior on touchscreens. Each `div` contains an image and applies a different `touch-action` class to illustrate its effect on touch interaction.

```html
<div class="h-48 w-full touch-auto overflow-auto ...">

</div>
<div class="h-48 w-full touch-none overflow-auto ...">
  <img class="h-auto w-[150%] max-w-none" src="..." />
</div>
<div class="h-48 w-full touch-pan-x overflow-auto ...">
  <img class="h-auto w-[150%] max-w-none" src="..." />
</div>

</div>

### Tailwind CSS: Complex Selectors Examples

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/styling-with-utility-classes

Illustrates the use of complex selectors in Tailwind CSS to style elements based on multiple conditions, such as dark mode, breakpoints, hover states, and data attributes. It provides examples of how to use variants like dark, hover, and data attributes to create dynamic styles.

```HTML
<button class="dark:lg:data-current:hover:bg-indigo-600 ...">  <!-- ... --></button>
```

```HTML
<a href="#" class="group rounded-lg p-8">  <!-- ... -->  <span class="group-hover:underline">Read more…</span></a>
```

```HTML
<div class="[&>[data-active]+span]:text-blue-600 ...">  <span data-active><!-- ... --></span>  <span>This text will be blue</span></div>
```

### Enable Tailwind CSS watcher in Phoenix development

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/phoenix

Add the Tailwind watcher to your `config/dev.exs` file. This configuration enables live reloading of your CSS during development, automatically recompiling Tailwind styles whenever changes are detected.

```elixir
watchers: [
  # Start the esbuild watcher by calling Esbuild.install_and_run(:default, args)
  esbuild: {Esbuild, :install_and_run, [:myproject, ~w(--sourcemap=inline --watch)]},
  tailwind: {Tailwind, :install_and_run, [:myproject, ~w(--watch)]}
]
```

### align-self Start - Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/align-self

Aligns a flex item to the start of the container's cross axis, overriding the container's align-items value. Use the self-start class to position items at the beginning of the cross axis.

```html
<div class="flex items-stretch ...">
  <div>01</div>
  <div class="self-start ...">02</div>
  <div>03</div>
</div>
```

---

### Apply `prefix()` to Tailwind CSS Theme and Utilities Imports (CSS)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/preflight

This example demonstrates applying a prefix, such as `prefix(tw)`, to both `tailwindcss/theme.css` and `tailwindcss/utilities.css` imports. This prefixes all generated utility classes and variables, preventing conflicts with existing CSS.

```css
@layer theme, base, components, utilities;
@import "tailwindcss/theme.css" layer(theme);
@import "tailwindcss/utilities.css" layer(utilities);
@import "tailwindcss/theme.css" layer(theme) prefix(tw);
@import "tailwindcss/utilities.css" layer(utilities) prefix(tw);
```

Apply styles below a specific container size using max-width container query variants like @max-sm and @max-md. This example changes flex direction from row to column when the container is smaller than md size.

```html
<div class="@container">
  <div class="flex flex-row @max-md:flex-col">
    <!-- ... -->
  </div>
</div>
```

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/min-width

---

### Stacking Arbitrary and Built-in Variants in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example illustrates the flexibility of arbitrary variants by stacking them with built-in Tailwind CSS variants. Here, the `[&.is-dragging]` arbitrary variant is combined with the `:active` pseudo-class to apply a `cursor-grabbing` style only when an element is both dragging and actively clicked/tapped.

```html
<ul role="list">
  {#each items as item}
  <li class="[&.is-dragging]:active:cursor-grabbing">{item}</li>
  {/each}
</ul>
```

### Basic text-underline-offset HTML Examples

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/text-underline-offset

Demonstrates using underline-offset utility classes with different numeric values (1, 2, 4, 8) to control text underline spacing. The underline class must be applied alongside the offset utility to display the underline effect.

```html
<p class="underline underline-offset-1">The quick brown fox...</p>
<p class="underline underline-offset-2">The quick brown fox...</p>
<p class="underline underline-offset-4">The quick brown fox...</p>
<p class="underline underline-offset-8">The quick brown fox...</p>
```

---

### CSS Variable Resolution Scope Issue Example

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/theme

Demonstrates how CSS variables resolve at their definition point rather than usage point, causing fallback values to be used unexpectedly when variables are not defined in the same scope.

```html
<div id="parent" style="--font-sans: var(--font-inter, sans-serif);">
  <div id="child" style="--font-inter: Inter; font-family: var(--font-sans);">
    This text will use the sans-serif font, not Inter.
  </div>
</div>
```

---

### Apply Tailwind CSS break-after utilities for basic column breaks

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/break-after

This example demonstrates how to use the `break-after-column` utility to force a column break after a specific paragraph within a multi-column layout. It shows the basic application of `break-after` utilities in HTML to control content flow.

```html
<div class="columns-2">
  <p>Well, let me tell you something, ...</p>
  <p class="break-after-column">Sure, go ahead, laugh...</p>
  <p>Maybe we can live without...</p>
  <p>Look. If you think this is...</p>
</div>
```

---

### Apply `source()` to Tailwind CSS Utilities Import (CSS)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/preflight

This example demonstrates how to apply the `source()` function, such as `source(none)`, to the `tailwindcss/utilities.css` import. This function affects how generated utilities are processed, for instance, by disabling source detection.

```css
@layer theme, base, components, utilities;
@import "tailwindcss/theme.css" layer(theme);
@import "tailwindcss/utilities.css" layer(utilities);
@import "tailwindcss/utilities.css" layer(utilities) source(none);
```

  <!-- ... -->
</div>

### Create Responsive Marketing Component Layout with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

This HTML snippet illustrates a responsive marketing page component using Tailwind CSS. It demonstrates how to achieve a stacked layout on small screens and a side-by-side layout on larger screens using `md:flex` and other responsive utilities. It also shows how to control image shrinking and sizing conditionally.

```html
<div
  class="mx-auto max-w-md overflow-hidden rounded-xl bg-white shadow-md md:max-w-2xl"
>
  <div class="md:flex">
    <div class="md:shrink-0">
      <img
        class="h-48 w-full object-cover md:h-full md:w-48"
        src="/img/building.jpg"
        alt="Modern building architecture"
      />
    </div>
    <div class="p-8">
      <div
        class="text-sm font-semibold tracking-wide text-indigo-500 uppercase"
      >
        Company retreats
      </div>
      <a
        href="#"
        class="mt-1 block text-lg leading-tight font-medium text-black hover:underline"
      >
        Incredible accommodation for your team
      </a>
      <p class="mt-2 text-gray-500">
        Looking to take your team away on a retreat to enjoy awesome food and
        take in some sunshine? We have a list of places to do just that.
      </p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div>
```

### Create Linear Gradients with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/background-image

Illustrates various linear gradient applications using Tailwind CSS utilities. Examples include gradients directed to the right, top, bottom-left, and at a specific angle, combining direction utilities with color stop definitions.

```html
<div class="h-14 bg-linear-to-r from-cyan-500 to-blue-500"></div>
<div class="h-14 bg-linear-to-t from-sky-500 to-indigo-500"></div>
<div class="h-14 bg-linear-to-bl from-violet-500 to-fuchsia-500"></div>
<div class="h-14 bg-linear-65 from-purple-500 to-pink-500"></div>
```

### Configure PostCSS Loader in Rspack

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/rspack/react

Enable PostCSS loader in the Rspack configuration file to process CSS files. This configuration routes CSS files through the PostCSS loader for plugin processing.

```typescript
export default defineConfig({
  // ...
  module: {
    rules: [
      {
        test: /\.css$/,
        use: ["postcss-loader"],
        type: "css",
      },
      // ...
    ],
  },
});
```

### Customize container sizes with Tailwind CSS theme variables

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

Add custom container query variants by defining theme variables in your CSS configuration. This example creates a new `8xl` container variant with a width of 96rem that can be applied to responsive layouts.

```css
@import "tailwindcss";
@theme {
  --container-8xl: 96rem;
}
```

### Implement Subgrid Columns with Tailwind CSS `grid-cols-subgrid`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/grid-template-columns

This example illustrates the use of the Tailwind CSS `grid-cols-subgrid` utility. It shows how a nested grid can adopt the column tracks defined by its parent, allowing for more complex and aligned layouts within a larger grid structure.

```html
<div class="grid grid-cols-4 gap-4">
  <div>01</div>
  <!-- ... -->
  <div>05</div>
  <div class="col-span-3 grid grid-cols-subgrid gap-4">
    <div class="col-start-2">06</div>
  </div>
</div>
```

### Globally link main.css in nuxt.config.ts for Nuxt

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/nuxt

This update to `nuxt.config.ts` adds the path to your `main.css` file to the global `css` array. By doing so, Nuxt automatically includes your Tailwind CSS styles across all pages and components of your application, ensuring consistent styling.

```typescript
import tailwindcss from "@tailwindcss/vite";
export default defineNuxtConfig({
  compatibilityDate: "2025-07-15",
  devtools: { enabled: true },
  css: ["./app/assets/css/main.css"],
  vite: {
    plugins: [tailwindcss()],
  },
});
```

### Configure Tailwind CSS PostCSS plugin

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/emberjs

Creates a `postcss.config.mjs` file in the project root to define PostCSS plugins. This configuration adds `@tailwindcss/postcss` to the plugin list, enabling Tailwind CSS processing for your stylesheets.

export default {
  plugins: {
    "@tailwindcss/postcss": {},
  },

### Use Arbitrary Breakpoint Values

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

Generate one-off breakpoints on the fly using min and max variants with arbitrary values in square brackets. This approach is useful for custom breakpoints that don't warrant adding to the theme configuration.

```html
<div class="max-[600px]:bg-sky-300 min-[320px]:text-center"><!-- ... --></div>
```

---

### Use arbitrary container query values in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

Apply one-off container query sizes using arbitrary value syntax without adding them to your theme. This example uses `@min-[475px]` to conditionally apply flex-row styling at a specific container width.

```html
<div class="@container">
  <div class="flex flex-col @min-[475px]:flex-row">
    <!-- ... -->
  </div>
</div>
```

### Apply Custom Line Clamping in HTML with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/line-clamp

This example demonstrates using the `line-clamp-[<value>]` syntax to define a custom number of lines for text clamping, allowing for dynamic values like CSS `calc()` functions. It also shows the shorthand `line-clamp-(<custom-property>)` for applying clamping based on a CSS variable, providing flexible control over text truncation.

```html
<p class="line-clamp-[calc(var(--characters)/100)] ...">
  Lorem ipsum dolor sit amet...
</p>
```

```html
<p class="line-clamp-(--my-line-count) ...">Lorem ipsum dolor sit amet...</p>
```

---

### Left Mask Gradient From Percentage - Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-image

Applies a left mask gradient starting from a specified percentage position. Transitions from black at the percentage to transparent on the right side.

```css
mask-image: linear-gradient(
  to left,
  black <percentage>,
  transparent var(--tw-mask-left-to)
);
```

### Update Phoenix deployment script for Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/phoenix

Modify the `assets.deploy` alias in `mix.exs` to include the Tailwind CSS build step for production deployments. This ensures that your CSS is minified and prepared correctly when deploying your Phoenix application.

```elixir
defp aliases do  [
    # …
    "assets.deploy": [
      "tailwind myproject --minify",
      "esbuild myproject --minify",
      "phx.digest"
    ]
  ]end
```

### Configure Tailwind CSS Vite Plugin

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/adonisjs

Add the @tailwindcss/vite plugin to the Vite configuration file. This integrates Tailwind CSS processing into the AdonisJS build pipeline alongside the AdonisJS Vite plugin.

```typescript
import { defineConfig } from "vite";
import adonisjs from "@adonisjs/vite/client";
import tailwindcss from "@tailwindcss/vite";

export default defineConfig({
  plugins: [
    tailwindcss(),
    adonisjs({
      // …
    }),
  ],
});
```

```css
mask-image: linear-gradient(
  to bottom,
  black var(--tw-mask-bottom-from),
  transparent <percentage>
);
```

  <div>02</div>
  <div>03</div>
</div>
```

```html

  <div>01</div>
  <div>02</div>
  <div>03</div>
</div>

### Use CSS variables in CSS Modules for improved performance

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/compatibility

Illustrates an alternative approach for styling in CSS modules using native CSS variables instead of `@apply`. This method bypasses Tailwind's processing for these specific styles, leading to better build performance and avoiding the need for explicit global style imports.

```css
button {
  background: var(--color-blue-500);
}
```

### Defining custom @supports variants in Tailwind CSS configuration

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example shows how to configure custom `@supports` variants in Tailwind CSS, allowing developers to create reusable shortcuts for common `@supports` rules. These custom variants can then be used directly in HTML.

```css
@custom-variant supports-grid {
  @supports (display: grid) {
    @slot;
  }
}
```

<button class="ring-4 ...">Subscribe</button>

<h1 class="text-3xl font-bold underline">

</h1>

    background-color: theme(--color-gray-100);
  }
</style>

### Apply Responsive Width Utilities to Images in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

This HTML example shows how to apply responsive width utilities from Tailwind CSS to an image. By using `w-16` for default width, `md:w-32` for medium screens, and `lg:w-48` for large screens, the image's size adapts to different viewport sizes. This demonstrates conditional styling based on breakpoints.

```html
<!-- Width of 16 by default, 32 on medium screens, and 48 on large screens --><img
  class="w-16 md:w-32 lg:w-48"
  src="..."
/>
```

### Importing Default Tailwind CSS Layers

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/theme

This CSS snippet shows the standard import structure for Tailwind CSS, demonstrating how it layers theme, base, components, and utilities. This is the foundational setup when including Tailwind CSS in a project.

```css
@layer theme, base, components, utilities;
@import "./theme.css" layer(theme);
@import "./preflight.css" layer(base);
@import "./utilities.css" layer(utilities);
```

### Share Theme Variables Across Projects

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/theme

Create a shared CSS file containing theme variables that can be imported into multiple projects. This approach works well in monorepo setups or when publishing theme packages to NPM.

```css
@theme {
  --*: initial;
  --spacing: 4px;
  --font-body: Inter, sans-serif;
  --color-lagoon: oklch(0.72 0.11 221.19);
  --color-coral: oklch(0.74 0.17 40.24);
  --color-driftwood: oklch(0.79 0.06 74.59);
  --color-tide: oklch(0.49 0.08 205.88);
  --color-dusk: oklch(0.82 0.15 72.09);
}
```

Creates a left mask gradient with a custom color at the starting point. Replaces black with a specified color for color-based left-side masking effects.

mask-image: linear-gradient(
  to left,
  <color> var(--tw-mask-left-from),

);

### Apply Negative 2D Rotation with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/rotate

This example shows how to apply counter-clockwise 2D rotations to image elements using Tailwind CSS `-rotate-<number>` utilities such as `-rotate-45`, `-rotate-90`, and `-rotate-210`.

```html
<img class="-rotate-45 ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" /><img
  class="-rotate-90 ..."
  src="/img/mountains.jpg"
/><img class="-rotate-210 ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
```

### Configure Vite Plugin for Tailwind CSS v4

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Migrate from PostCSS plugin to the dedicated Vite plugin for improved performance and better developer experience. This is the recommended approach for Vite-based projects in v4.

```typescript
import { defineConfig } from "vite";
import tailwindcss from "@tailwindcss/vite";

export default defineConfig({
  plugins: [tailwindcss()],
});
```

```html
<div class="flex [@supports(display:grid)]:grid"><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Target Breakpoint Range with Responsive and Max Variants

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

```html
<div class="md:max-xl:flex"><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Explicitly setting sort order with order-<number> utilities

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/order

```html

  <div class="order-3 ...">01</div>
  <div class="order-1 ...">02</div>
  <div class="order-2 ...">03</div>
</div>

### Apply perspective utilities to 3D transformed elements

```html
<div class="size-20 perspective-dramatic ...">
  <div class="translate-z-12 rotate-x-0 bg-sky-300/75 ...">1</div>
  <div class="-translate-z-12 rotate-y-18 bg-sky-300/75 ...">2</div>
  <div class="translate-x-12 rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">3</div>
  <div class="-translate-x-12 -rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">4</div>
  <div class="-translate-y-12 rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">5</div>
  <div class="translate-y-12 -rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">6</div>
</div>
<div class="size-20 perspective-normal ...">
  <div class="translate-z-12 rotate-x-0 bg-sky-300/75 ...">1</div>
  <div class="-translate-z-12 rotate-y-18 bg-sky-300/75 ...">2</div>
  <div class="translate-x-12 rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">3</div>
  <div class="-translate-x-12 -rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">4</div>
  <div class="-translate-y-12 rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">5</div>
  <div class="translate-y-12 -rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">6</div>
</div>

### Basic HTML structure with Tailwind CSS classes

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/parcel

This HTML snippet demonstrates a fundamental page structure, linking to the compiled CSS file and applying Tailwind CSS utility classes to an `<h1>` element. The classes `text-3xl`, `font-bold`, and `underline` are used to style the heading, showcasing basic Tailwind integration.

```HTML
<!doctype html>
<html>
  <head>
    <meta charset="UTF-8" />
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0" />
    <link href="./index.css" type="text/css" rel="stylesheet" />
  </head>
  <body>
    <h1 class="text-3xl font-bold underline">
      Hello world!
    </h1>
  </body>
</html>
```

);

### Create Inline Flex Container in HTML/CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/display

This example showcases the `inline-flex` utility in Tailwind CSS, which creates an inline-level flex container. Unlike `flex`, `inline-flex` allows the container itself to flow with surrounding text, while its children are still laid out using flexbox rules. The snippet integrates a small profile image and name within a paragraph of text, demonstrating how `inline-flex` maintains text flow.

```html
<p>
  Today I spent most of the day researching ways to ...
  <span class="inline-flex items-baseline">
    <img src="/img/kramer.jpg" class="mx-1 size-5 self-center rounded-full" />
    <span>Kramer</span>
  </span>
  keeps telling me there is no way to make it work, that ...
</p>
```

### justify-self-center - Center grid item horizontally

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/justify-self

Centers a grid item along the center of its inline axis. The safe variant (justify-self-center-safe) will align to the start if insufficient space is available, preventing content overflow.

```html
<div class="grid justify-items-stretch ...">
  <!-- ... -->
  <div class="justify-self-center ...">02</div>
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

```html
<div class="grid justify-items-stretch ...">
  <!-- ... -->
  <div class="justify-self-center-safe ...">02</div>
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

---

### Left Mask Gradient From Spacing Number - Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-image

Creates a left-to-right mask gradient starting from a spacing-based numeric value. Uses calc() to multiply the spacing variable for consistent design system alignment.

```css
mask-image: linear-gradient(
  to left,
  black calc(var(--spacing) * <number>),
  transparent var(--tw-mask-left-to)
);
```

### Import application stylesheet into Ember.js app entry

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/emberjs

Modifies the `./app/app.js` file to import the newly created `./app/app.css` file. This ensures that the main application stylesheet, containing Tailwind CSS, is loaded and applied when the Ember.js application initializes.

```javascript
import Application from "@ember/application";
import Resolver from "ember-resolver";
import loadInitializers from "ember-load-initializers";
import config from "my-project/config/environment";
import "my-project/app.css";
export default class App extends Application {
  modulePrefix = config.modulePrefix;
  podModulePrefix = config.podModulePrefix;
  Resolver = Resolver;
}
loadInitializers(App, config.modulePrefix);
```

### Enable PostCSS support in Ember CLI build configuration

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/emberjs

Modifies the `ember-cli-build.js` file to configure Webpack within Embroider. This configuration ensures that `postcss-loader` processes all `.css` files, allowing PostCSS and Tailwind CSS to be applied during the build.

```javascript
'use strict';const EmberApp = require('ember-cli/lib/broccoli/ember-app');module.exports = function (defaults) {  const app = new EmberApp(defaults, {    // Add options here  });  const { Webpack } = require('@embroider/webpack');  return require('@embroider/compat').compatBuild(app, Webpack, {    skipBabel: [      {        package: 'qunit',      },    ],    packagerOptions: {      webpackConfig: {        module: {          rules: [            {              test: /\.css$/i,              use: ['postcss-loader'],            },          ],        },      },    },  });};
```

### Apply basic backdrop brightness filters with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/backdrop-filter-brightness

This example demonstrates how to use Tailwind CSS utility classes like `backdrop-brightness-50` and `backdrop-brightness-150` to control the backdrop brightness of an element. These classes apply predefined brightness levels to the `backdrop-filter` CSS property.

```html
<div class="bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)]">
  <div class="bg-white/30 backdrop-brightness-50 ..."></div>
</div>
<div class="bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)]">
  <div class="bg-white/30 backdrop-brightness-150 ..."></div>
</div>
```

---

### Apply responsive backdrop contrast with Tailwind CSS breakpoints

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/backdrop-filter-contrast

Use breakpoint variants like md: to apply backdrop-contrast utilities only at specific screen sizes. This example applies backdrop-contrast-125 by default and backdrop-contrast-150 at medium screen sizes and above.

```html
<div class="backdrop-contrast-125 md:backdrop-contrast-150 ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

---

### Justify Center - Align Items to Container Center

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/justify-content

Use the justify-center utility to align flex items along the center of the container's main axis. The justify-center-safe variant will align items to the start if insufficient space is available.

```html
<div class="flex justify-center ...">
  <div>01</div>
  <div>02</div>
  <div>03</div>
  <div>04</div>
</div>
```

```html
<div class="flex justify-center-safe ...">
  <div>01</div>
  <div>02</div>
  <div>03</div>
  <div>04</div>
</div>
```

---

### Left Mask Gradient From Arbitrary Value - Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-image

Creates a left mask gradient with an arbitrary custom value for the starting point. Allows direct specification of any valid CSS value for the left mask position.

```css
mask-image: linear-gradient(
  to left,
  black <value>,
  transparent var(--tw-mask-left-to)
);
```

---

### Generated CSS for Tailwind Responsive Breakpoint Utility

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/styling-with-utility-classes

This example displays the CSS generated by Tailwind for the `sm:grid-cols-3` utility class. It shows how breakpoint variants are transformed into standard CSS `@media` queries, applying styles conditionally based on the viewport width.

```css
.sm\:grid-cols-3 {
  @media (width >= 40rem) {
    grid-template-columns: repeat(3, minmax(0, 1fr));
  }
}
```

### Configure Tailwind CSS Vite plugin in Astro config

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/astro

This configuration snippet adds the `@tailwindcss/vite` plugin to the `vite.plugins` array within the `astro.config.mjs` file. This enables Tailwind CSS processing during the Astro build. It imports `defineConfig` from `astro/config` and `tailwindcss` from `@tailwindcss/vite`.

```javascript
// @ts-check
import { defineConfig } from "astro/config";
import tailwindcss from "@tailwindcss/vite";

// https://astro.build/config
export default defineConfig({
  vite: {
    plugins: [tailwindcss()],
  },
});
```

---

### Conic Gradient Mask - Angle and Color Configuration

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-image

Create conic gradient masks using utilities like mask-conic-<number>, mask-conic-from-<value>, and mask-conic-to-<value>. These utilities generate conic-gradient mask-image values with customizable starting angles, colors, and gradient stops.

```css
mask-image: conic-gradient(
  from 50deg,
  black var(--tw-mask-conic-from),
  transparent var(--tw-mask-conic-to)
);
mask-image: conic-gradient(
  from calc(50deg * -1),
  black var(--tw-mask-conic-from),
  transparent var(--tw-mask-conic-to)
);
mask-image: conic-gradient(
  from var(--tw-mask-conic-position),
  black 20%,
  transparent var(--tw-mask-conic-to)
);
mask-image: conic-gradient(
  from var(--tw-mask-conic-position),
  #ff0000 var(--tw-mask-conic-from),
  transparent var(--tw-mask-conic-to)
);
```

### Responsive transition-duration with breakpoint variants

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/transition-duration

Apply different transition durations at different screen sizes using Tailwind breakpoint variants. This example sets duration-0 by default and changes to duration-150 at medium screen sizes and above using the md: prefix.

```html
<button class="duration-0 md:duration-150 ..."><!-- ... --></button>
```

Style an element when the user hovers over it with the mouse cursor. This example uses the `hover` variant to change the background color of a div from black to white on hover.

```html
<div class="bg-black hover:bg-white ..."><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Repeat mask image vertically with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-repeat

This example demonstrates how to use the `mask-repeat-y` utility to repeat a mask image only along the vertical axis. It requires a mask image URL and size for the mask to be applied.

```html
<div
  class="mask-repeat-y mask-[url(/img/circle.png)] mask-size-[50px_50px] bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)]..."
></div>

### Apply Tailwind classes in CSS Modules using @reference

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/compatibility

Demonstrates how to use `@apply` within a CSS module by explicitly importing global styles with `@reference`. This ensures that Tailwind's theme variables are available for processing, allowing features like `@apply` to function as expected in isolated CSS module contexts.

```css
@reference "../app.css";
button {
  @apply bg-blue-500;
}
```

### Control Grid Column Start/End with Tailwind CSS `col-start`/`col-end`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/grid-column

Illustrates the use of `col-start-<number>` and `col-end-<number>` utilities in Tailwind CSS to position elements at specific grid lines. This example combines these with `col-span-<number>` to precisely place and size elements within a 6-column grid, showcasing advanced grid placement.

```html
<div class="grid grid-cols-6 gap-4">
  <div class="col-span-4 col-start-2 ...">01</div>
  <div class="col-start-1 col-end-3 ...">02</div>
  <div class="col-span-2 col-end-7 ...">03</div>
  <div class="col-start-1 col-end-7 ...">04</div>
</div>

### Create Block Formatting Context with Flow Root in HTML/CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/display

This example illustrates the use of the `flow-root` utility in Tailwind CSS to create a block-level element that establishes its own block formatting context. This is useful for containing floats without needing to clear them explicitly, ensuring that the parent element correctly encloses its floated children. The snippet shows two `div` elements, each using `flow-root` to manage their internal content.

```html
<div class="p-4">
  <div class="flow-root ...">
    <div class="my-4 ...">Well, let me tell you something, ...</div>
  </div>
  <div class="flow-root ...">
    <div class="my-4 ...">Sure, go ahead, laugh if you want...</div>
  </div>
</div>
```

### Customize Animation Theme with CSS Variables

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/animation

Demonstrates how to define custom animations in the theme configuration using `--animate-*` CSS variables and `@keyframes`. This creates reusable animation utilities that can be applied throughout the project.

```css
@theme {
  --animate-wiggle: wiggle 1s ease-in-out infinite;
  @keyframes wiggle {
    0%,
    100% {
      transform: rotate(-3deg);
    }
    50% {
      transform: rotate(3deg);
    }
  }
}
```

### Create Block-Level Flex Container in HTML/CSS

The example shows a simple layout for a profile card, aligning an image and text content horizontally.

### Use --spacing() in arbitrary values with calc()

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/functions-and-directives

Combine the --spacing() function with calc() in arbitrary values for precise spacing calculations. This is useful for fine-tuning spacing with pixel adjustments.

```HTML
<div class="py-[calc(--spacing(4)-1px)]">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

---

### Vertical Y-Axis Mask Gradient From Color - Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-image

Creates a Y-axis mask gradient with custom colors at both top and bottom starting points. Uses intersect composite mode to combine the two directional gradients.

```css
mask-image:
  linear-gradient(
    to top,
    <color> var(--tw-mask-top-from),
    transparent var(--tw-mask-top-to)
  ),
  linear-gradient(
    to bottom,
    <color> var(--tw-mask-bottom-from),
    transparent var(--tw-mask-bottom-to)
  );
mask-composite: intersect;
```

---

### Apply directional border radius (start) with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/border-radius

Tailwind CSS utilities for applying border-radius to start-side corners (logical direction). Supports predefined scales, custom properties, and arbitrary values for inline-start and block-start corners.

```css
/* Start-side directional radius */
.rounded-s-xs {
  border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-xs); /* 0.125rem (2px) */
  border-end-start-radius: var(--radius-xs); /* 0.125rem (2px) */
}
.rounded-s-sm {
  border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-sm); /* 0.25rem (4px) */
  border-end-start-radius: var(--radius-sm); /* 0.25rem (4px) */
}
.rounded-s-md {
  border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-md); /* 0.375rem (6px) */
  border-end-start-radius: var(--radius-md); /* 0.375rem (6px) */
}
.rounded-s-lg {
  border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-lg); /* 0.5rem (8px) */
  border-end-start-radius: var(--radius-lg); /* 0.5rem (8px) */
}
.rounded-s-xl {
  border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-xl); /* 0.75rem (12px) */
  border-end-start-radius: var(--radius-xl); /* 0.75rem (12px) */
}
.rounded-s-2xl {
  border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-2xl); /* 1rem (16px) */
  border-end-start-radius: var(--radius-2xl); /* 1rem (16px) */
}
.rounded-s-3xl {
  border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-3xl); /* 1.5rem (24px) */
  border-end-start-radius: var(--radius-3xl); /* 1.5rem (24px) */
}
.rounded-s-4xl {
  border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-4xl); /* 2rem (32px) */
  border-end-start-radius: var(--radius-4xl); /* 2rem (32px) */
}
.rounded-s-none {
  border-start-start-radius: 0;
  border-end-start-radius: 0;
}
.rounded-s-full {
  border-start-start-radius: calc(infinity * 1px);
  border-end-start-radius: calc(infinity * 1px);
}
.rounded-s-(<custom-property>) {
  border-start-start-radius: var(<custom-property>);
  border-end-start-radius: var(<custom-property>);
}
.rounded-s-[<value>] {
  border-start-start-radius: <value>;
  border-end-start-radius: <value>;
}
```

### Import Tailwind CSS and define source paths in app.css

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/laravel/vite

This CSS import statement brings in Tailwind's base styles, components, and utilities. The `@source` directives instruct Tailwind CSS which files to scan for utility classes, ensuring that only used styles are included in the final build.

```css
@import "tailwindcss";
@source '../../vendor/laravel/framework/src/Illuminate/Pagination/resources/views/*.blade.php';
@source '../../storage/framework/views/*.php';
@source '../**/*.blade.php';
@source '../**/*.js';
```

```html
<img class="scale-[1.7] ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
```

```html
<img class="scale-(--my-scale) ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
```

### Apply High Contrast Styles with Tailwind CSS `contrast-more` Variant

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example demonstrates using the `contrast-more` variant to apply specific styles when the user has requested more contrast through the `prefers-contrast` media query. It allows for adjusting elements like borders, placeholders, and text opacity to enhance readability for users with contrast preferences.

```html
<label class="block">
  <span class="block text-sm font-medium text-gray-700"
    >Social Security Number</span
  >
  <input
    class="border-gray-200 placeholder-gray-400 contrast-more:border-gray-400 contrast-more:placeholder-gray-500 ..."
  />
  <p class="text-gray-600 opacity-10 contrast-more:opacity-100 ...">
    We need this to steal your identity.
  </p>
</label>
```

### Clear Left Utility - Tailwind CSS HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/clear

Positions an element below any preceding left-floated elements using the clear-left utility class. This is useful when you have floated images or elements on the left side and need text or other content to start below them.

```html

### Configure Tailwind CSS Vite Plugin in nuxt.config.ts

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/nuxt

This configuration snippet adds the `@tailwindcss/vite` plugin to the `vite.plugins` array within your `nuxt.config.ts` file. It ensures that Tailwind CSS is properly recognized and processed by Vite, which Nuxt uses for its build system, allowing for correct compilation of Tailwind utilities.

```typescript
import tailwindcss from "@tailwindcss/vite";
export default defineNuxtConfig({
  compatibilityDate: "2025-07-15",
  devtools: { enabled: true },
  vite: {
    plugins: [tailwindcss()],
  },
});
```

### Run Tailwind CSS Upgrade Tool

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Execute the official Tailwind CSS upgrade tool to automate the migration process from v3 to v4. This tool handles dependency updates, configuration file migration to CSS, and template file changes. Requires Node.js 20 or higher.

```bash
npx @tailwindcss/upgrade
```

### Basic Container Query with @container Class

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

Mark an element as a container using @container class, then use container query variants like @sm and @md to style children based on container size rather than viewport size. Container queries are mobile-first like breakpoint variants.

```html
<div class="@container">
  <div class="flex flex-col @md:flex-row">
    <!-- ... -->
  </div>
</div>
```

```html

  <a href="#" class="ml-2 first-of-type:ml-6 ..."> <!-- ... --> </a> {/each}
</nav>

### Implement Subgrid with Tailwind CSS `grid-rows-subgrid`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/grid-template-rows

This example shows how to use the `grid-rows-subgrid` utility in Tailwind CSS to make a nested grid item adopt the row tracks defined by its parent. This allows for more complex grid layouts where child elements align with the parent's grid.

```html
<div class="grid grid-flow-col grid-rows-4 gap-4">
  <div>01</div>
  <!-- ... -->
  <div>05</div>
  <div class="row-span-3 grid grid-rows-subgrid gap-4">
    <div class="row-start-2">06</div>
  </div>
  <div>07</div>
  <!-- ... -->
  <div>10</div>
</div>
```

---

### Sort Tailwind CSS classes with Prettier plugin

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/editor-setup

Official Prettier plugin that automatically sorts Tailwind CSS utility classes in HTML following the recommended class order. Works with custom Tailwind configurations and integrates with all editors that support Prettier.

```html
<!-- Before -->
<button
  class="text-white px-4 sm:px-8 py-2 sm:py-3 bg-sky-700 hover:bg-sky-800"
>
  Submit
</button>

<!-- After -->
<button
  class="bg-sky-700 px-4 py-2 text-white hover:bg-sky-800 sm:px-8 sm:py-3"
>
  Submit
</button>
```

### Applying print-specific styles with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example uses the `print` variant in Tailwind CSS to apply styles exclusively when the document is being printed. It can be used to hide certain elements from printouts or display print-specific messages.

```html
<div>
  <article class="print:hidden">
    <h1>My Secret Pizza Recipe</h1>
    <p>This recipe is a secret, and must not be shared with anyone</p>
    <!-- ... -->
  </article>
  <div class="hidden print:block">
    Are you seriously trying to print this? It's secret!
  </div>
</div>
```

### Create Grid Container in HTML/CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/display

This snippet illustrates the use of the `grid` utility in Tailwind CSS to create a block-level grid container. Applying `grid` enables CSS Grid layout for the element's direct children, allowing for complex two-dimensional layouts. The example sets up a 3x3 grid with gaps, ready for content placement.

```html
<div class="grid grid-cols-3 grid-rows-3 gap-4"><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Use CSS variables in Vue/Svelte/Astro scoped styles for performance

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/compatibility

Presents a performance-optimized way to style components in Vue, Svelte, or Astro using native CSS variables within scoped `<style>` blocks. This approach avoids Tailwind's processing overhead for these styles, improving build times and eliminating the need for `@reference` imports.

```html
<template>
  <button><slot /></button>
</template>
<style scoped>
  button {
    background-color: var(--color-blue-500);
  }
</style>
```

```html
<div class="py-4 md:py-8 ..."><!-- ... --></div>

### Define Custom Shorthand Variants in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/adding-custom-styles

This example illustrates the shorthand syntax for defining custom variants in Tailwind CSS using the `@custom-variant` directive. This concise method is suitable when complex nesting is not required, providing a simpler way to create variants like `theme-midnight:`.

```css
@custom-variant theme-midnight (&:where([data-theme="midnight"] *));
```

### Migrate from Tailwind CSS `space-y` to Flex/Grid `gap` (v4 HTML)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Provides an alternative migration strategy for Tailwind CSS v4 `space-x-*` and `space-y-*` utilities if the selector change causes issues. It recommends migrating to a flex or grid layout and using the `gap` utility for spacing instead.

```html
<div class="space-y-4 p-4">
  <div class="flex flex-col gap-4 p-4">
    <label for="name">Name</label>
    <input type="text" name="name" />
  </div>
</div>
```

### Configure theme variables with prefix in Tailwind CSS v4

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

When using a prefix, configure theme variables as if no prefix is used. The generated CSS variables will automatically include the prefix to prevent conflicts with existing project variables.

```css
@import "tailwindcss" prefix(tw);

@theme {
  --font-display: "Satoshi", "sans-serif";
  --breakpoint-3xl: 120rem;
  --color-avocado-100: oklch(0.99 0 0);
  --color-avocado-200: oklch(0.98 0.04 113.22);
  --color-avocado-300: oklch(0.94 0.11 115.03);
  /* ... */
}
```

### Safelisting Tailwind CSS Utilities with Ranges and Variants

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/detecting-classes-in-source-files

This example demonstrates the advanced use of `@source inline()` with brace expansion and ranges to efficiently generate multiple utility classes and their variants. It generates a range of red background colors (e.g., `bg-red-100` to `bg-red-900`) including specific shades and their `hover` variants.

```CSS
@import "tailwindcss";@source inline("{hover:,}bg-red-{50,{100..900..100},950}");
```

```CSS
.bg-red-50 {  background-color: var(--color-red-50);}
.bg-red-100 {  background-color: var(--color-red-100);}
.bg-red-200 {  background-color: var(--color-red-200);}
/* ... */
.bg-red-800 {  background-color: var(--color-red-800);}
.bg-red-900 {  background-color: var(--color-red-900);}
.bg-red-950 {  background-color: var(--color-red-950);}
@media (hover: hover) {  .hover\:bg-red-50:hover {    background-color: var(--color-red-50);  }  /* ... */  .hover\:bg-red-950:hover {    background-color: var(--color-red-950);  }}
```

### Configure Vite plugin for Tailwind CSS in SolidJS `vite.config.ts`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/solidjs

Modifies the `vite.config.ts` file to include the `@tailwindcss/vite` plugin, enabling Tailwind CSS processing within the Vite build pipeline. It also configures the SolidJS plugin and server settings for development.

```TypeScript
import { defineConfig } from 'vite';import solidPlugin from 'vite-plugin-solid';import tailwindcss from '@tailwindcss/vite';export default defineConfig({
  plugins: [
    tailwindcss(),
    solidPlugin(),
  ],
  server: {
    port: 3000,
  },
  build: {
    target: 'esnext',
  },
});
```

### Configure Tailwind CSS in Laravel Mix webpack.mix.js

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/laravel/mix

Add Tailwind CSS as a PostCSS plugin in the webpack.mix.js configuration file. This tells Laravel Mix to process your CSS files through the Tailwind CSS PostCSS plugin during the build process.

```javascript
mix
  .js("resources/js/app.js", "public/js")
  .postCss("resources/css/app.css", "public/css", [
    require("@tailwindcss/postcss"),
  ]);
```

### Replace Commas with Underscores in Grid and Object Position - HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Update grid-cols-_, grid-rows-_, and object-\* utilities to use underscores instead of commas for spaces in arbitrary values. The v3 comma-to-space conversion compatibility has been removed in v4.

```html
<div class="grid-cols-[max-content_auto]"></div>
```

  to bottom,
  black var(<custom-property>),
  transparent var(--tw-mask-bottom-to)
);
```

```css
@import "tailwindcss";
@source not "../../public";
```

### Configure Vite to use Tailwind CSS and React Router plugins

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/react-router

This configuration file (`vite.config.ts`) integrates the `@tailwindcss/vite` and `@react-router/dev/vite` plugins into the Vite build process. It ensures that both Tailwind CSS processing and React Router development tools are properly set up for the project.

```typescript
import { reactRouter } from "@react-router/dev/vite";
import { defineConfig } from "vite";
import tsconfigPaths from "vite-tsconfig-paths";
import tailwindcss from "@tailwindcss/vite";

export default defineConfig({
  plugins: [tailwindcss(), reactRouter(), tsconfigPaths()],
});
```

### Apply Tailwind CSS mask-position utilities for basic positioning

This example demonstrates how to use predefined Tailwind CSS classes like `mask-top-left`, `mask-center`, and `mask-bottom-right` to control the position of an element's mask image. It shows various combinations applied to `div` elements, along with `mask-[url(...)]` and `mask-size-[...]` for a complete masking effect.

<div
  class="mask-center mask-[url(/img/circle.png)] mask-size-[50%] bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)] ..."
></div>

></div>

></div>
