### justify-self-end - Align grid item to inline end

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/justify-self

Aligns a grid item to the end of its inline axis within the grid area. The safe variant (justify-self-end-safe) will align to the start if insufficient space is available, preventing content overflow.

```html
<div class="grid justify-items-stretch ...">
  <!-- ... -->
  <div class="justify-self-end ...">02</div>
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

```html
<div class="grid justify-items-stretch ...">
  <!-- ... -->
  <div class="justify-self-end-safe ...">02</div>
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Place important modifier at end of class name in Tailwind CSS v4

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

In v4, the important modifier `!` is placed at the very end of the class name instead of at the beginning. The old syntax is still supported for compatibility but is deprecated.

```html
<div class="flex! bg-red-500! hover:bg-red-600/50!"><!-- ... --></div>
```

```html

  <!-- ... -->
</button>
```

### Remove default CSS import from Phoenix JavaScript

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/phoenix

Remove the default CSS import line from `assets/js/app.js`. Since Tailwind is now handling your styling pipeline, this default import is no longer needed and can be safely removed to avoid conflicts or redundant processing.

```javascript
// Remove this line if you add your own CSS build pipeline (e.g postcss).import "../css/app.css"
```

### Apply Basic Backdrop Invert Filters with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/backdrop-filter-invert

This example demonstrates the fundamental usage of Tailwind CSS `backdrop-invert` utilities. It shows how to apply no inversion (`backdrop-invert-0`), partial inversion (`backdrop-invert-65`), and full inversion (`backdrop-invert`) to an element's backdrop, typically used with a semi-transparent background.

```html
<div class="bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)]">
  <div class="bg-white/30 backdrop-invert-0 ..."></div>
</div>
<div class="bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)]">
  <div class="bg-white/30 backdrop-invert-65 ..."></div>
</div>
<div class="bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)]">
  <div class="bg-white/30 backdrop-invert ..."></div>
</div>
```

### Nest Multiple Tailwind Variants in Custom CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/adding-custom-styles

Combine multiple Tailwind variants using nested @variant directives to apply complex styling conditions. This example demonstrates dark mode combined with hover state.

```css
.my-element {
  background: white;
  @variant dark {
    @variant hover {
      background: black;
    }
  }
}
```

### Tailwind CSS: Using Arbitrary Values

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/styling-with-utility-classes

Demonstrates the use of arbitrary values in Tailwind CSS to apply custom styles that are not part of the default theme. This includes setting custom colors, grid layouts, and CSS features like calc(). The examples show how to use square bracket syntax to define these values directly in class names.

```HTML
<button class="bg-[#316ff6] ...">  Sign in with Facebook</button>
```

```HTML
<div class="grid grid-cols-[24rem_2.5rem_minmax(0,1fr)]">  <!-- ... --></div>
```

```HTML
<div class="max-h-[calc(100dvh-(--spacing(6)))]">  <!-- ... --></div>
```

```HTML
<div class="[--gutter-width:1rem] lg:[--gutter-width:2rem]">  <!-- ... --></div>
```

### Translate elements along the y-axis with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/translate

This example demonstrates translating elements solely along the vertical (y) axis using Tailwind CSS `translate-y-<number>` or `translate-y-<fraction>` utilities. It includes instances of positive and negative y-axis translations.

```html
<img class="-translate-y-4 ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" /><img
  class="translate-y-2 ..."
  src="/img/mountains.jpg"
/><img class="translate-y-1/2 ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
```

### Support Fractional Values with `ratio` Data Type in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/adding-custom-styles

This example demonstrates how to handle fractional values in Tailwind CSS utilities by utilizing the CSS `ratio` data type with `--value()`. Using `ratio` signals Tailwind to treat the value and modifier as a single unit, enabling utilities like `aspect-3/4` and `aspect-[7/9]` for aspect ratios.

```css
@utility aspect-* {
  aspect-ratio: --value(--aspect-ratio-*, ratio, [ratio]);
}
```

### Manual Hyphenation with Tailwind CSS `hyphens-manual`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hyphens

This example illustrates the use of the `hyphens-manual` utility class in Tailwind CSS. It allows words to be hyphenated only at explicitly defined soft hyphen (`&shy;`) points, giving precise control over line breaks. This behavior is often the default in browsers.

```html
<p class="hyphens-manual">
  ... Kraftfahrzeug&shy;haftpflichtversicherung is a ...
</p>
```

### Styling All Descendants with Tailwind CSS `**` Variant

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example demonstrates the `**` variant, which applies styles to all descendant elements, not just direct children. It's especially powerful when combined with other variants, like data attributes, to target specific elements deep within the DOM structure.

```html
<ul class="**:data-avatar:size-12 **:data-avatar:rounded-full ...">
  {#each items as item}
  <li>
    <img src="{item.src}" data-avatar />
    <p>{item.name}</p>
  </li>
  {/each}
</ul>
```

---

### Flatten nested CSS with Tailwind

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/compatibility

Tailwind uses Lightning CSS to process nested CSS syntax and automatically flattens it for browser compatibility. Nested selectors are converted to standard CSS that works across all modern browsers.

```css
.typography {
  p {
    font-size: var(--text-base);
  }
  img {
    border-radius: var(--radius-lg);
  }
}
```

```css
.typography p {
  font-size: var(--text-base);
}
.typography img {
  border-radius: var(--radius-lg);
}
```

### Bottom Mask Gradient From Color - Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-image

Creates a bottom mask gradient with a custom color at the starting point. Replaces black with a specified color value while maintaining transparency at the bottom endpoint using CSS custom variables.

```css
mask-image: linear-gradient(
  to bottom,
  <color> var(--tw-mask-bottom-from),
  transparent var(--tw-mask-bottom-to)
);
```

```html

  <time>Mar 10, 2020</time>
  <h2>Boost your conversion rate</h2>
  <p class="line-clamp-3">

    labore enim adipisicing minim ad. Est in quis eu dolore occaecat excepteur
    fugiat dolore nisi aliqua fugiat enim ut cillum. Labore enim duis nostrud
    eu. Est ut eiusmod consequat irure quis deserunt ex. Enim laboris dolor
```

### Vertical Y-Axis Mask Gradient From Custom Property - Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-image

Applies a Y-axis mask gradient using custom CSS properties for both top and bottom starting positions. Enables dynamic symmetric vertical masking through CSS variables.

```css
mask-image:
  linear-gradient(
    to top,
    black var(<custom-property>),
    transparent var(--tw-mask-top-to)
  ),
  linear-gradient(
    to bottom,
    black var(<custom-property>),
    transparent var(--tw-mask-bottom-to)
  );
mask-composite: intersect;
```

The snippet shows two inline grid containers, each displaying a 3x2 grid of numbered spans, flowing horizontally within a line.

```html
  <span>05</span> <span>06</span></span
><span class="inline-grid grid-cols-3 gap-4">

  <span>05</span> <span>06</span></span
>
```

### React Button with Multiple Color Variants

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/detecting-classes-in-source-files

Extended React component example showing how to map different prop values to different color shades using a colorVariants object. This pattern allows for flexible component styling while maintaining static class name detection for Tailwind's build process.

```JSX
function Button({ color, children }) {
  const colorVariants = {
    blue: "bg-blue-600 hover:bg-blue-500 text-white",
    red: "bg-red-500 hover:bg-red-400 text-white",
    yellow: "bg-yellow-300 hover:bg-yellow-400 text-black",
  };
  return <button className={`${colorVariants[color]} ...`}>{children}</button>;
}
```

---

### Avoid Incorrect Mobile Text Centering with Tailwind CSS `sm:` Prefix

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

This HTML example highlights a common mistake when targeting mobile screens with Tailwind CSS. Using `sm:text-center` will only apply text centering on screens 640px and wider, not on smaller mobile screens. It serves as a caution against misinterpreting the `sm:` prefix as 'small screens' rather than 'at the small breakpoint and above'.

```html
<!-- This will only center text on screens 640px and wider, not on small screens -->
<div class="sm:text-center"></div>
```

### Apply Tailwind CSS Arbitrary Peers with Custom Selectors

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This HTML example demonstrates using arbitrary values with `peer-*` variants to create one-off styles based on custom selectors. The `peer-[.is-dirty]:peer-required:block` class applies styles when the sibling `input` has both the `is-dirty` class and is required, providing fine-grained control over sibling-based styling.

```html
<form>
  <label for="email">Email:</label>
  <input id="email" name="email" type="email" class="is-dirty peer" required />
  <div class="peer-[.is-dirty]:peer-required:block hidden">
    This field is required.
  </div>
  <!-- ... -->
</form>
```

### Generated CSS variables with prefix in Tailwind CSS v4

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

CSS variables generated with a prefix automatically include the prefix namespace to avoid conflicts. Variables are prefixed with the specified prefix (e.g., `--tw-` for `prefix(tw)`).

```css
:root {
  --tw-font-display: "Satoshi", "sans-serif";
  --tw-breakpoint-3xl: 120rem;
  --tw-color-avocado-100: oklch(0.99 0 0);
  --tw-color-avocado-200: oklch(0.98 0.04 113.22);
  --tw-color-avocado-300: oklch(0.94 0.11 115.03);
  /* ... */
}
```

### Use prefix syntax in Tailwind CSS v4 class names

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Prefixes in v4 now look like variants and appear at the beginning of class names. Apply the prefix to all utility classes while configuring theme variables without the prefix to avoid conflicts.

```html
<div class="tw:flex tw:bg-red-500 tw:hover:bg-red-600"><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Apply Tailwind classes in Vue/Svelte/Astro scoped styles using @reference

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/compatibility

Shows how to use `@apply` within a component's scoped `<style>` block in frameworks like Vue, Svelte, or Astro. Similar to CSS modules, an `@reference` import of global styles is necessary to provide the context for Tailwind's `@apply` directive to work correctly.

```html
<template>
  <button><slot /></button>
</template>
<style scoped>
  @reference "../app.css";
  button {
    @apply bg-blue-500;
  }
</style>
```

### Apply responsive field-sizing with breakpoint variants - Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/field-sizing

Use breakpoint prefixes like md: to conditionally apply field-sizing utilities at specific screen sizes. This example applies content-based sizing on mobile and switches to fixed sizing at medium breakpoints and above.

```html
<input class="field-sizing-content md:field-sizing-fixed ..." />
```

### Applying Custom Flex Grow Values with Tailwind CSS `grow-[<value>]`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/flex-grow

Demonstrates the `grow-[<value>]` syntax for setting arbitrary `flex-grow` values in Tailwind CSS. This allows for highly specific control over an item's growth using any valid CSS unit or keyword.

```html
<div class="grow-[25vw] ..."><!-- ... --></div>
```

---

### Define component utilities with @utility API in Tailwind CSS v4

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Component utilities defined with `@utility` are sorted by property count, allowing them to be overridden by other Tailwind utilities without additional configuration. This replaces the v3 `@layer components` approach.

```css
@layer components {
  .btn {
    border-radius: 0.5rem;
    padding: 0.5rem 1rem;
    background-color: ButtonFace;
  }
}

@utility btn {
  border-radius: 0.5rem;
  padding: 0.5rem 1rem;
  background-color: ButtonFace;
}
```

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/background-origin

This snippet illustrates how to apply `background-origin` utilities responsively using breakpoint variants. By prefixing a utility with `md:`, the `background-origin` property will only be applied at medium screen sizes and above, allowing for adaptive designs based on viewport dimensions.

```html
<div class="bg-origin-border md:bg-origin-padding ..."><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Apply nth-of-type styles with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

Style an element at a specific position, of the same type, using the `nth-of-type` variant. This example uses `nth-of-type-3` and `nth-of-type-[3n+1]` to apply horizontal margins to `a` tags based on their position among `a` siblings.

```html
<nav>
  <img src="/logo.svg" alt="Vandelay Industries" /> {#each links as link}
  <a href="#" class="mx-2 nth-of-type-3:mx-6 nth-of-type-[3n+1]:mx-7 ...">
    <!-- ... -->
  </a>
  {/each} <button>More</button>
</nav>
```

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/white-space

This example demonstrates the `whitespace-pre-line` utility class in Tailwind CSS, which preserves newlines but collapses multiple spaces into single spaces. Text will wrap normally within the HTML element, respecting the original line breaks.

```html

  Hey everyone!It's almost 2022 and we still don't know if there are aliens
  living among us, or do we? Maybe the person writing this is an alien.You will
  never know.
</p>
```

### Apply mask-alpha utility with gradient mask in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-mode

Demonstrates using the mask-alpha utility to control mask visibility based on opacity. The example combines mask-alpha with radial gradient mask utilities (mask-r-from-black, mask-r-to-transparent) and a background image. The opacity of the mask determines which parts of the element are visible.

```html
<div
  class="mask-alpha mask-r-from-black mask-r-from-50% mask-r-to-transparent bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)] ..."
></div>
```

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Describes how to customize the `container` utility in Tailwind CSS v4, as v3's configuration options like `center` and `padding` are no longer available. It demonstrates using the `@utility` directive to apply custom styles such as `margin-inline` and `padding-inline`.

```css
@utility container {
  margin-inline: auto;
  padding-inline: 2rem;
}
```

```html
<p class="overflow-auto whitespace-pre">
```

### Border Inline Start Color - Stone Palette

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/border-color

Applies border-inline-start-color using the stone color palette in Tailwind CSS. Supports 10 predefined shades from stone-100 (lightest) to stone-950 (darkest), with OKLCH color space values for modern color accuracy.

```css
.border-s-stone-100 {
  border-inline-start-color: var(--color-stone-100);
  /* oklch(97% 0.001 106.424) */
}

.border-s-stone-200 {
  border-inline-start-color: var(--color-stone-200);
  /* oklch(92.3% 0.003 48.717) */
}

.border-s-stone-300 {
  border-inline-start-color: var(--color-stone-300);
  /* oklch(86.9% 0.005 56.366) */
}

.border-s-stone-400 {
  border-inline-start-color: var(--color-stone-400);
  /* oklch(70.9% 0.01 56.259) */
}

.border-s-stone-500 {
  border-inline-start-color: var(--color-stone-500);
  /* oklch(55.3% 0.013 58.071) */
}

.border-s-stone-600 {
  border-inline-start-color: var(--color-stone-600);
  /* oklch(44.4% 0.011 73.639) */
}

.border-s-stone-700 {
  border-inline-start-color: var(--color-stone-700);
  /* oklch(37.4% 0.01 67.558) */
}

.border-s-stone-800 {
  border-inline-start-color: var(--color-stone-800);
  /* oklch(26.8% 0.007 34.298) */
}

.border-s-stone-900 {
  border-inline-start-color: var(--color-stone-900);
  /* oklch(21.6% 0.006 56.043) */
}

.border-s-stone-950 {
  border-inline-start-color: var(--color-stone-950);
  /* oklch(14.7% 0.004 49.25) */
}
```

```html
></div>
```

### Apply basic mask-origin utilities in HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-origin

This HTML snippet demonstrates how to apply different `mask-origin` utilities like `mask-origin-border`, `mask-origin-padding`, and `mask-origin-content` to `div` elements. It shows how to control where an element's mask image is rendered relative to its box model, using a circular mask and a background image for visual effect.

```html
<div
  class="mask-origin-border border-3 p-1.5 mask-[url(/img/circle.png)] bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)] ..."
></div>
<div
  class="mask-origin-padding border-3 p-1.5 mask-[url(/img/circle.png)] bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)] ..."
></div>
<div
  class="mask-origin-content border-3 p-1.5 mask-[url(/img/circle.png)] bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)] ..."
></div>
```

This example demonstrates how to use predefined Tailwind CSS `brightness-<number>` utilities to adjust the brightness of an image. Different classes like `brightness-50`, `brightness-100`, `brightness-125`, and `brightness-200` are applied to control the image's luminosity, directly setting the `filter: brightness()` CSS property.

```html
  class="brightness-100 ..."
  src="/img/mountains.jpg"
```

```html
>

</div>
```

### Incorrect Dynamic Class Names in HTML Templates

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/detecting-classes-in-source-files

Anti-pattern example demonstrating dynamic class name construction in HTML templates using conditional expressions. Tailwind cannot parse these expressions, so the resulting class names like 'text-red-600' and 'text-green-600' will not be generated.

```HTML
<div class="text-{{ error ? 'red' : 'green' }}-600"></div>
```

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

```html
<input type="checkbox" class="appearance-none checked:bg-blue-500 ..." />
```

### Tailwind CSS Accent Color Utility Class Reference

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/accent-color

This section provides a comprehensive reference of Tailwind CSS utility classes for setting the `accent-color` property. It includes predefined color palettes (gray, zinc, neutral, stone) with their corresponding CSS output and OKLCH color values, as well as examples for using custom properties and arbitrary values.

```css
accent-color: var(--color-gray-900); /* oklch(21% 0.034 264.665) */
accent-color: var(--color-gray-950); /* oklch(13% 0.028 261.692) */
accent-color: var(--color-zinc-50); /* oklch(98.5% 0 0) */
accent-color: var(--color-zinc-100); /* oklch(96.7% 0.001 286.375) */
accent-color: var(--color-zinc-200); /* oklch(92% 0.004 286.32) */
accent-color: var(--color-zinc-300); /* oklch(87.1% 0.006 286.286) */
accent-color: var(--color-zinc-400); /* oklch(70.5% 0.015 286.067) */
accent-color: var(--color-zinc-500); /* oklch(55.2% 0.016 285.938) */
accent-color: var(--color-zinc-600); /* oklch(44.2% 0.017 285.786) */
accent-color: var(--color-zinc-700); /* oklch(37% 0.013 285.805) */
accent-color: var(--color-zinc-800); /* oklch(27.4% 0.006 286.033) */
accent-color: var(--color-zinc-900); /* oklch(21% 0.006 285.885) */
accent-color: var(--color-zinc-950); /* oklch(14.1% 0.005 285.823) */
accent-color: var(--color-neutral-50); /* oklch(98.5% 0 0) */
accent-color: var(--color-neutral-100); /* oklch(97% 0 0) */
accent-color: var(--color-neutral-200); /* oklch(92.2% 0 0) */
accent-color: var(--color-neutral-300); /* oklch(87% 0 0) */
accent-color: var(--color-neutral-400); /* oklch(70.8% 0 0) */
accent-color: var(--color-neutral-500); /* oklch(55.6% 0 0) */
accent-color: var(--color-neutral-600); /* oklch(43.9% 0 0) */
accent-color: var(--color-neutral-700); /* oklch(37.1% 0 0) */
accent-color: var(--color-neutral-800); /* oklch(26.9% 0 0) */
accent-color: var(--color-neutral-900); /* oklch(20.5% 0 0) */
accent-color: var(--color-neutral-950); /* oklch(14.5% 0 0) */
accent-color: var(--color-stone-50); /* oklch(98.5% 0.001 106.423) */
accent-color: var(--color-stone-100); /* oklch(97% 0.001 106.424) */
accent-color: var(--color-stone-200); /* oklch(92.3% 0.003 48.717) */
accent-color: var(--color-stone-300); /* oklch(86.9% 0.005 56.366) */
accent-color: var(--color-stone-400); /* oklch(70.9% 0.01 56.259) */
accent-color: var(--color-stone-500); /* oklch(55.3% 0.013 58.071) */
accent-color: var(--color-stone-600); /* oklch(44.4% 0.011 73.639) */
accent-color: var(--color-stone-700); /* oklch(37.4% 0.01 67.558) */
accent-color: var(--color-stone-800); /* oklch(26.8% 0.007 34.298) */
accent-color: var(--color-stone-900); /* oklch(21.6% 0.006 56.043) */
accent-color: var(--color-stone-950); /* oklch(14.7% 0.004 49.25) */
accent-color: var(<custom-property>);

```

### Center dialog elements with margin auto in Tailwind CSS v4

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Preflight now resets margins on dialog elements for consistency. Add this CSS to your base layer to restore the v3 behavior of centering dialogs by default using `margin: auto`.

```css
@layer base {
  dialog {
    margin: auto;
  }
}
```

### Set Custom Transform Origin Value in HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/transform-origin

This example shows how to use the arbitrary value syntax `origin-[<value>]` to set a custom `transform-origin` for an HTML element. The `origin-[33%_75%]` class applies a specific percentage-based origin to the image, allowing for precise control over the transformation pivot point.

```html
<img class="origin-[33%_75%] ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
```

---

### Resetting Element Margins and Padding with Preflight CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/preflight

This Preflight CSS rule removes all default margins and padding from common elements like `*`, `::after`, `::before`, `::backdrop`, and `::file-selector-button`. This ensures a consistent starting point for spacing, preventing reliance on browser-default margin values.

```css
*,
::after,
::before,
::backdrop,
::file-selector-button {
  margin: 0;
  padding: 0;
}
```

```html
<div class="backdrop-contrast-[.25] ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Traditional CSS for Button Hover State Styling

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/styling-with-utility-classes

This example contrasts Tailwind's approach with traditional CSS for styling button hover states. It shows how a single `.btn` class in conventional CSS would typically define both default and hover styles using nested selectors within a `<style>` block.

```html
<button class="btn">Save changes</button
><style>
  .btn {
    background-color: var(--color-sky-500);
    &:hover {
      background-color: var(--color-sky-700);
    }
  }
</style>
```

---

### Bottom Mask Gradient From Percentage - Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-image

Creates a bottom-to-top mask gradient starting from a specified percentage. Uses linear-gradient with black at the percentage point transitioning to transparent at the bottom. Applies CSS mask-image property with CSS custom variables for dynamic control.

```css
mask-image: linear-gradient(
  to bottom,
  black <percentage>,
  transparent var(--tw-mask-bottom-to)
);
```

---

### Mask X-Axis From Gradient - Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-image

Creates horizontal gradient masks starting from left and right edges with configurable opacity points. Supports numeric multipliers of spacing scale, percentages, colors, custom properties, and arbitrary values for flexible gradient positioning.

```css
/* Numeric variant */
mask-image:
  linear-gradient(
    to right,
    black calc(var(--spacing) * <number>),
    transparent var(--tw-mask-right-to)
  ),
  linear-gradient(
    to left,
    black calc(var(--spacing) * <number>),
    transparent var(--tw-mask-left-to)
  );
mask-composite: intersect;
```

```css
/* Percentage variant */
mask-image:
  linear-gradient(
    to right,
    black <percentage>,
    transparent var(--tw-mask-right-to)
  ),
  linear-gradient(
    to left,
    black <percentage>,
    transparent var(--tw-mask-left-to)
  );
mask-composite: intersect;
```

```css
/* Color variant */
mask-image:
  linear-gradient(
    to right,
    <color> var(--tw-mask-right-from),
    transparent var(--tw-mask-right-to)
  ),
  linear-gradient(
    to left,
    <color> var(--tw-mask-left-from),
    transparent var(--tw-mask-left-to)
  );
mask-composite: intersect;
```

```css
/* Custom property variant */
mask-image:
  linear-gradient(
    to right,
    black var(<custom-property>),
    transparent var(--tw-mask-right-to)
  ),
  linear-gradient(
    to left,
    black var(<custom-property>),
    transparent var(--tw-mask-left-to)
  );
mask-composite: intersect;
```

```css
/* Arbitrary value variant */
mask-image:
  linear-gradient(to right, black <value>, transparent var(--tw-mask-right-to)),
  linear-gradient(to left, black <value>, transparent var(--tw-mask-left-to));
mask-composite: intersect;
```

---

### Incorrect Dynamic Class Name Construction in React

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/detecting-classes-in-source-files

Anti-pattern example showing how NOT to construct Tailwind classes dynamically using template literals and props. This approach fails because Tailwind cannot detect the resulting class names during the scanning phase, resulting in missing CSS generation.

```JSX
function Button({ color, children }) {
  return <button className={`bg-${color}-600 hover:bg-${color}-500 ...`}>{children}</button>;
}
```

---

### Apply transform-style utilities in HTML with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/transform-style

Demonstrates the usage of transform-3d and transform-flat classes to control 3D space positioning of child elements. The example shows two containers with identical child elements positioned differently based on the transform-style utility applied. The transform-3d class enables 3D transformations while transform-flat restricts to 2D space.

```html
<div class="size-20 transform-flat ...">
  <div class="translate-z-12 rotate-x-0 bg-sky-300/75 ...">1</div>
  <div class="-translate-z-12 rotate-y-18 bg-sky-300/75 ...">2</div>
  <div class="translate-x-12 rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">3</div>
  <div class="-translate-x-12 -rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">4</div>
  <div class="-translate-y-12 rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">5</div>
  <div class="translate-y-12 -rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">6</div>
</div>
<div class="size-20 transform-3d ...">
  <div class="translate-z-12 rotate-x-0 bg-sky-300/75 ...">1</div>
  <div class="-translate-z-12 rotate-y-18 bg-sky-300/75 ...">2</div>
  <div class="translate-x-12 rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">3</div>
  <div class="-translate-x-12 -rotate-y-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">4</div>
  <div class="-translate-y-12 rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">5</div>
  <div class="translate-y-12 -rotate-x-90 bg-sky-300/75 ...">6</div>
</div>
```

### Applying styles when a condition is not true using Tailwind CSS `not-` variant

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This section illustrates the use of the `not-` variant to apply styles when a specified condition is false. It shows examples combining `not-` with pseudo-class variants like `hover` and media query variants such as `supports` to achieve conditional styling.

```html
<button class="bg-indigo-600 hover:not-focus:bg-indigo-700">
  <!-- ... -->
</button>
```

```html
<div class="not-supports-[display:grid]:flex"><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Apply Accent Color on Hover with Tailwind CSS Variants

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/accent-color

This example illustrates how to conditionally apply an accent color using Tailwind CSS variants, specifically `hover:accent-pink-500`. This allows the accent color of an element, such as a checkbox, to change dynamically when the user hovers over it, providing interactive feedback.

```html
<input class="accent-black hover:accent-pink-500" type="checkbox" />
```

---

### Named Container Queries for Complex Layouts

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

Use named containers with @container/{name} syntax to target specific containers in complex nested layouts. This allows styling based on distant container sizes rather than just the nearest parent container.

```html
<div class="@container/main">
  <!-- ... -->
  <div class="flex flex-row @sm/main:flex-col">
    <!-- ... -->
  </div>
</div>
```

### Apply Custom CSS Variable Transform with Tailwind CSS `transform-(<custom-property>)`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/transform

This example demonstrates how to apply a transform based on a custom CSS variable using the `transform-(<custom-property>)` shorthand in Tailwind CSS. This utility automatically wraps the custom property in `var()`, providing a concise way to use dynamic transform values.

```html
<div class="transform-(--my-transform) ..."><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Build Responsive Card Component with Tailwind Utilities

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/styling-with-utility-classes

A complete notification card component demonstrating layout, spacing, typography, and dark mode utilities. Uses flex layout, padding, max-width constraints, rounded corners, shadows, and responsive text styling. Includes dark mode variants with dark: prefix for theme-aware styling.

```html
<div
  class="mx-auto flex max-w-sm items-center gap-x-4 rounded-xl bg-white p-6 shadow-lg outline outline-black/5 dark:bg-slate-800 dark:shadow-none dark:-outline-offset-1 dark:outline-white/10"
>
  <img class="size-12 shrink-0" src="/img/logo.svg" alt="ChitChat Logo" />

    <div class="text-xl font-medium text-black dark:text-white">ChitChat</div>

  </div>
</div>
```

### Apply nth-last-child styles with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

Style an element at a specific position from the end using the `nth-last` variant. This example shows `nth-last-3` and `nth-last-[3n+1]` to apply horizontal margins to `a` tags based on their position counting from the end of their siblings.

```html
<nav>
  <img src="/logo.svg" alt="Vandelay Industries" /> {#each links as link}
  <a href="#" class="mx-2 nth-last-3:mx-6 nth-last-[3n+1]:mx-7 ...">
    <!-- ... -->
  </a>
  {/each} <button>More</button>
</nav>
```

### Correct Static Class Names in HTML Templates

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/detecting-classes-in-source-files

Best practice example showing how to use complete, static class names in HTML templates with conditional expressions. By placing the entire class name inside the conditional, Tailwind can detect both possible class names during the scanning phase.

```HTML
<div class="{{ error ? 'text-red-600' : 'text-green-600' }}"></div>
```

### Apply Inset Shadow Utilities in HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/box-shadow

Use inset-shadow utilities with size variants (2xs, xs, sm) to apply inset box shadows to elements. Opacity can be adjusted using modifiers like /50 to control shadow visibility.

```html
<div class="inset-shadow-2xs ..."></div>
<div class="inset-shadow-xs ..."></div>
<div class="inset-shadow-sm ..."></div>
```

### Preventing Hyphenation with Tailwind CSS `hyphens-none`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hyphens

This example demonstrates how to use the `hyphens-none` utility class in Tailwind CSS to prevent words from being hyphenated, even when soft hyphens (`&shy;`) are present. This ensures text remains unhyphenated, overriding browser defaults for line breaking.

```html
<p class="hyphens-none">
  ... Kraftfahrzeug&shy;haftpflichtversicherung is a ...
</p>
```

### Apply Negative Scroll Padding with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/scroll-padding

This HTML snippet demonstrates how to apply a negative scroll padding value using Tailwind CSS. The `-scroll-ps-6` utility sets a negative `scroll-padding-inline-start` value on the element, potentially causing content to scroll further than its natural start.

```html
<div class="-scroll-ps-6 snap-x ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Apply percentage-based min-height in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/min-height

Use min-h-full or min-h-<fraction> utilities like min-h-1/2, min-h-3/4, and min-h-9/10 to set minimum heights as percentages of the parent container.

```html
<div class="min-h-full ...">min-h-full</div>
<div class="min-h-9/10 ...">min-h-9/10</div>
<div class="min-h-3/4 ...">min-h-3/4</div>
<div class="min-h-1/2 ...">min-h-1/2</div>
<div class="min-h-1/3 ...">min-h-1/3</div>
```

### Apply Image Mask with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-image

Use the mask-[<value>] syntax to set a custom mask image on an element. This example applies a scribble pattern mask to an element with a mountain background image. The mask image path is specified using the bracket notation for arbitrary values.

```html
<div class="mask-[url(/img/scribble.png)] bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)] ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Basic background-clip utilities - HTML/Tailwind CSS

Demonstrates the three basic background-clip utilities (border, padding, content) applied to bordered div elements with indigo background. Each utility controls where the background extends relative to the element's box model.

```html
<div class="border-4 bg-indigo-500 bg-clip-border p-3"></div>
<div class="border-4 bg-indigo-500 bg-clip-padding p-3"></div>
```

### Style Default Form Elements with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example demonstrates how to style an option, checkbox, or radio button that was the default value when the page initially loaded, using the `default` variant in Tailwind CSS. It applies an outline to the default checked checkbox.

```html
<input type="checkbox" class="default:outline-2 ..." />
```

---

### Collapse Table Rows/Columns with Tailwind CSS `collapse`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/visibility

This example illustrates the use of the `collapse` utility class in Tailwind CSS for hiding table rows or columns. It effectively hides the element as if `display: none` was applied, but without impacting the size or layout of other rows and columns in the table, enabling dynamic toggling without layout shifts.

```html
<table>
  <thead>
    <tr>
      <th>Invoice #</th>
      <th>Client</th>
      <th>Amount</th>
    </tr>
  </thead>
  <tbody>
    <tr>
      <td>#100</td>
      <td>Pendant Publishing</td>
      <td>$2,000.00</td>
    </tr>
    <tr class="collapse">
      <td>#101</td>
      <td>Kruger Industrial Smoothing</td>
      <td>$545.00</td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
      <td>#102</td>
      <td>J. Peterman</td>
      <td>$10,000.25</td>
    </tr>
  </tbody>
</table>
```

---

### Apply Tailwind CSS ::before Pseudo-element for Decorative Text Styling

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This HTML example uses the `before:` variant to create a decorative background effect for a word within a quote. A `<span>` with `before:absolute before:-inset-1 before:block before:-skew-y-3 before:bg-pink-500` creates a skewed background rectangle, demonstrating how pseudo-elements can be used for visual enhancements without adding extra DOM elements.

```html
<blockquote
  class="text-center text-2xl font-semibold text-gray-900 italic dark:text-white"
>
  When you look
  <span
    class="relative inline-block before:absolute before:-inset-1 before:block before:-skew-y-3 before:bg-pink-500"
  >
    <span class="relative text-white dark:text-gray-950">annoyed</span>
  </span>
  all the time, people think that you're busy.
</blockquote>
```

### Reverse divide direction for reversed flex layouts

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/border-width

When child elements are in reverse order using flex-row-reverse or flex-col-reverse, use divide-x-reverse or divide-y-reverse utilities to ensure borders appear on the correct side. This example uses divide-y-4 with divide-y-reverse for a reversed column layout.

```html
<div class="flex flex-col-reverse divide-y-4 divide-y-reverse divide-gray-200">
  <div>01</div>
  <div>02</div>
  <div>03</div>
</div>
```

### Adjusting color opacity with Tailwind CSS utility classes

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/colors

This HTML snippet illustrates how to control the opacity of a background color using Tailwind CSS's `/` syntax. It demonstrates applying varying opacity levels (from 10% to 100%) to a base color (`bg-sky-500`), showcasing how to create translucent effects directly within utility classes.

```html
<div>
  <div class="bg-sky-500/10"></div>
  <div class="bg-sky-500/20"></div>
  <div class="bg-sky-500/30"></div>

  <div class="bg-sky-500/50"></div>
  <div class="bg-sky-500/60"></div>
  <div class="bg-sky-500/70"></div>
  <div class="bg-sky-500/80"></div>
  <div class="bg-sky-500/90"></div>
  <div class="bg-sky-500/100"></div>
```

---

### Implement Hover Media Query for Touch Devices - CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

The hover variant now only applies when the primary input device supports hover, using @media (hover: hover). Override with @custom-variant if your site depends on touch devices triggering hover on tap, though this is not recommended.

```css
@media (hover: hover) {
  .hover\:underline:hover {
    text-decoration: underline;
  }
}
```

```css
@custom-variant hover (&:hover);
```

---

### Set Base Path for Source Detection with source()

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/detecting-classes-in-source-files

CSS function to explicitly set the base path for Tailwind's source file scanning, relative to the stylesheet. Useful in monorepo setups where build commands run from the root directory rather than individual project roots.

```CSS
@import "tailwindcss" source("../src");
```

### Apply Basic Tailwind CSS Transition Timing Functions

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/transition-timing-function

Demonstrates how to use predefined Tailwind CSS utilities like `ease-in`, `ease-out`, and `ease-in-out` to control the easing curve of an element's transition. These classes are applied directly to HTML elements, often alongside a `duration` utility.

```html
<button class="duration-300 ease-in ...">Button A</button
><button class="duration-300 ease-out ...">Button B</button
><button class="duration-300 ease-in-out ...">Button C</button>
```

```html
<div class="grid grid-cols-2 gap-4">

  <div>02</div>
  <div>03</div>
  <div>04</div>
```

### Reset Individual Transform Properties - HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Replace transform-none with individual property resets (scale-none, rotate-none, translate-none) since transform utilities are now based on individual CSS properties. The transform-none approach no longer works for resetting individual transform utilities.

```html
<button class="scale-150 focus:scale-none"></button>
```

### Apply fixed sizing to textarea - Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/field-sizing

Use the field-sizing-fixed utility class to maintain a fixed size for a form control regardless of content. This example shows a textarea with fixed width (w-80) and 2 rows that maintains its dimensions as text is entered.

```html
<textarea class="field-sizing-fixed w-80 ..." rows="2">
Latex Salesman, Vanderlay Industries</textarea
>
```

### Styling elements based on parent state with Tailwind CSS `group-*` variants

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example demonstrates how to style child elements based on the state of their parent. By applying the `group` class to the parent, child elements can use `group-*` variants (e.g., `group-hover`, `group-focus`) to react to the parent's state changes.

```html
<a href="#" class="group ...">
  <div>
    <svg
      class="stroke-sky-500 group-hover:stroke-white ..."
      fill="none"
      viewBox="0 0 24 24"
    >
      <!-- ... -->
    </svg>
    <h3 class="text-gray-900 group-hover:text-white ...">New project</h3>
  </div>
  <p class="text-gray-500 group-hover:text-white ...">
    Create a new project from a variety of starting templates.
  </p></a
>
```

### Include compiled CSS and use Tailwind classes in a Blade template

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/installation/framework-guides/laravel/vite

This HTML snippet demonstrates how to include the compiled CSS using Laravel's `@vite` directive and apply Tailwind CSS utility classes. It shows a basic `h1` element styled with `text-3xl`, `font-bold`, and `underline`.

```html
<!doctype html>
<html>
  <head>
    <meta charset="utf-8" />
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0" />
    @vite('resources/css/app.css')
  </head>
  <body>
    <h1 class="text-3xl font-bold underline">Hello world!</h1>
  </body>
</html>
```

### Update ring utility from 3px to 1px in Tailwind CSS v4

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Migrate ring utilities from v3 to v4 by replacing `ring` with `ring-3` and explicitly adding `ring-blue-500` to maintain the previous default blue color. The ring utility width changed from 3px to 1px and the default color changed from blue-500 to currentColor for consistency with other utilities.

```html
<button class="focus:ring ...">
  <button class="focus:ring-3 ..."><!-- ... --></button>
</button>
```

```html
<button class="focus:ring-3 focus:ring-blue-500 ..."><!-- ... --></button>
```

### Apply Backdrop Invert with CSS Variable in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/backdrop-filter-invert

This example demonstrates applying a `backdrop-filter: invert()` value using a CSS variable with Tailwind CSS. The `backdrop-invert-(<custom-property>)` syntax automatically wraps the custom property in `var()`, enabling dynamic inversion control via CSS variables.

```html
<div class="backdrop-invert-(--my-backdrop-inversion) ..."><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Styling Direct Children with Tailwind CSS `*` Variant

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example illustrates the use of the `*` variant to apply Tailwind CSS utility classes directly to all immediate child elements of a parent. This technique is particularly useful when you need to style children whose structure you don't directly control, such as content generated by a CMS or third-party component.

```html
<div>  <h2>Categories<h2>  <ul class="*:rounded-full *:border *:border-sky-100 *:bg-sky-50 *:px-2 *:py-0.5 dark:text-sky-300 dark:*:border-sky-500/15 dark:*:bg-sky-500/10 ...">    <li>Sales</li>    <li>Marketing</li>    <li>SEO</li>    <!-- ... -->  </ul></div>
```

### Applying styles based on viewport orientation with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example illustrates the use of Tailwind CSS `portrait` and `landscape` variants to conditionally apply styles when the viewport is in a specific orientation. It can be used to hide content or display messages based on the device's rotation.

```html
<div>
  <div class="portrait:hidden">
    <!-- ... -->
  </div>
  <div class="landscape:hidden">
    <p>
      This experience is designed to be viewed in landscape. Please rotate your
      device to view the site.
    </p>
  </div>
</div>
```

### Set Custom Accent Color with Arbitrary Values in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/accent-color

This example demonstrates using Tailwind CSS's arbitrary value syntax (`accent-[<value>]`) to apply a custom hexadecimal color value directly to the `accent-color` property of an input element. This method provides flexibility for precise color customization beyond the predefined color palette.

```html
<input class="accent-[#50d71e] ..." type="checkbox" />
```

### Extending Tailwind CSS Theme with a Custom Font

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/theme

This example demonstrates how to extend the default Tailwind CSS theme by defining a new custom font family variable (`--font-script`) within the `@theme` block in your `app.css`. This makes a new `font-script` utility class available for use in your HTML.

```css
@import "tailwindcss";
@theme {
  --font-script: Great Vibes, cursive;
}
```

---

### Apply Conditional Value Transformations in Tailwind CSS Utilities

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/adding-custom-styles

This snippet demonstrates how to use multiple `--value()` declarations in Tailwind CSS to apply different transformations based on the value type. For example, it shows how to convert a bare integer to a percentage for an `opacity` utility, allowing for distinct handling of different input formats.

```css
@utility opacity-* {
  opacity: --value([percentage]);
  opacity: calc(--value(integer) * 1%);
  opacity: --value(--opacity-*);
}
```

---

### Handle break spaces with Tailwind CSS `whitespace-break-spaces`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/white-space

This example illustrates the `whitespace-break-spaces` utility class in Tailwind CSS, which preserves newlines and spaces. Unlike `pre-wrap`, white space at the end of lines will not hang but will wrap to the next line, providing more controlled text flow, especially useful for code or pre-formatted text.

```html
<p class="whitespace-break-spaces">
  Hey everyone!It's almost 2022 and we still don't know if there are aliens
  living among us, or do we? Maybe the person writing this is an alien.You will
  never know.
</p>
```

Use arbitrary value syntax with scroll-margin utilities to apply completely custom scroll margin values. This example demonstrates using scroll-ml-[24rem] to set a custom left scroll margin on a div element.

```html
<div class="scroll-ml-[24rem] ..."><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Use Custom Themed Animation in Markup

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/animation

Shows how to use a custom animation utility that was defined in the theme configuration. Once defined, custom animations can be used like any built-in animation utility.

```html
<div class="animate-wiggle">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Apply Styles When Not in Forced Colors Mode with Tailwind CSS `not-forced-colors` Variant

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example demonstrates the `not-forced-colors` variant, which allows applying styles specifically when the user is _not_ using a forced colors mode. This can be useful for overriding default behaviors or ensuring certain styles only apply in standard color environments.

```html
<div class="not-forced-colors:appearance-none ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Custom Animation with Arbitrary Values

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/animation

Shows how to use the `animate-[<value>]` syntax to apply completely custom animation values directly in markup. This allows for one-off animations without requiring theme customization.

```html
<div class="animate-[wiggle_1s_ease-in-out_infinite] ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Set Outline Color Unconditionally for Transitions - HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

The transition and transition-colors utilities now include outline-color property. Set outline color unconditionally or explicitly for both states to prevent color transitions from default values when using custom outline colors on focus.

```html
<button class="outline-cyan-500 transition hover:outline-2"></button>
```

### Set Custom Outline Offset Value in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/outline-offset

This example shows how to define a custom outline offset value using arbitrary value syntax `outline-offset-[<value>]` in Tailwind CSS. It allows for precise control over the outline's position, such as `outline-offset-[2vw]`.

```html
<div class="outline-offset-[2vw] ..."><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Apply Tailwind CSS `odd` and `even` variants to table rows

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example illustrates how to use the `odd` and `even` pseudo-class variants in Tailwind CSS to apply alternating background colors to table rows. This enhances readability by visually distinguishing rows in a table, here demonstrated with a list of people's names, titles, and emails.

```html
<table>
  <!-- ... -->
  <tbody>
    {#each people as person}
    <!-- Use different background colors for odd and even rows -->
    <tr
      class="odd:bg-white even:bg-gray-50 dark:odd:bg-gray-900/50 dark:even:bg-gray-950"
    >
      <td>{person.name}</td>
      <td>{person.title}</td>
      <td>{person.email}</td>
    </tr>
    {/each}
  </tbody>
</table>
```

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/top-right-bottom-left

Shows how to use breakpoint prefixes like md: with positioning utilities to apply different position values at different screen sizes. Enables responsive design by conditionally applying positioning utilities at specific breakpoints.

```HTML
<div class="top-4 md:top-6 ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Manage Tailwind CSS Gradient Variant Overrides with `via-none` (v4 HTML)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Explains the improved gradient variant behavior in Tailwind CSS v4, where values are preserved. It shows how to explicitly 'unset' a three-stop gradient back to a two-stop gradient using `via-none` in a specific state, like `dark:via-none`.

```html
<div
  class="bg-linear-to-r from-red-500 via-orange-400 to-yellow-400 dark:via-none dark:from-blue-500 dark:to-teal-400"
>
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Use native CSS variables in Tailwind

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/compatibility

Modern browsers support native CSS variables without preprocessor tools. Tailwind relies heavily on CSS variables internally, allowing you to use var() syntax for dynamic styling with predefined custom properties.

```css
.typography {
  font-size: var(--text-base);
  color: var(--color-gray-700);
}
```

### Apply Border Start Color with Black and White in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/border-color

Utility classes for setting inline-start border color using black and white colors. The border-s-black and border-s-white classes apply the border-inline-start-color CSS property with predefined black (#000) and white (#fff) color variables for high-contrast border styling.

```css
/* border-s-black */
border-inline-start-color: var(--color-black); /* #000 */

/* border-s-white */
border-inline-start-color: var(--color-white); /* #fff */
```

### Applying Tailwind CSS color utility classes for UI elements

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/colors

This HTML example showcases the application of various Tailwind CSS color utility classes to style a UI component, such as a notification or message card. It demonstrates setting background colors (`bg-white`, `dark:bg-gray-800`), border colors (`border-pink-300`), and text colors (`text-gray-700`, `text-gray-950`) to create a visually appealing and responsive design.

```html
<div
  class="flex items-center gap-4 rounded-lg bg-white p-6 shadow-md outline outline-black/5 dark:bg-gray-800"
>
  <span
    class="inline-flex shrink-0 rounded-full border border-pink-300 bg-pink-100 p-2 dark:border-pink-300/10 dark:bg-pink-400/10"
  >
    <svg class="size-6 stroke-pink-700 dark:stroke-pink-500"><!-- ... --></svg>
  </span>

      mentioned you in
      <span class="font-medium text-gray-950 dark:text-white"
        >Logo redesign</span
      >
    </p>
    <time class="mt-1 block text-gray-500" datetime="9:37">9:37am</time>
  </div>
</div>
```

### Resolve Multiple Value Types with Single `--value()` in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/adding-custom-styles

This example shows that the `--value()` function in Tailwind CSS can accept multiple arguments to resolve theme, bare, and arbitrary values in a left-to-right order. This simplifies utility definitions when no special handling is needed for different types, as seen with `tab-size` and `opacity` utilities.

```css
@theme {
  --tab-size-github: 8;
}
@utility tab-* {
  tab-size: --value(--tab-size-*, integer, [integer]);
}
@utility opacity-* {
  opacity: calc(--value(integer) * 1%);
  opacity: --value(--opacity-*, [percentage]);
}
```

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/cursor

Demonstrates using the cursor-(<custom-property>) syntax as shorthand for cursor-[var(<custom-property>)] to reference CSS custom properties for cursor values.

```html
<button class="cursor-(--my-cursor) ..."><!-- ... --></button>
```

### Apply Border Start Color with Special Values in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/border-color

Utility classes for setting inline-start border color using special keyword values. The border-s-inherit, border-s-current, and border-s-transparent classes apply the border-inline-start-color CSS property with inherit, currentColor, and transparent values respectively for flexible border styling.

```css
/* border-s-inherit */
border-inline-start-color: inherit;

/* border-s-current */
border-inline-start-color: currentColor;

/* border-s-transparent */
border-inline-start-color: transparent;
```

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example demonstrates how to apply styles to an input element when its value falls outside a specified range, using the `out-of-range` variant in Tailwind CSS. It adds a red border to inputs with values outside the defined `min` and `max`.

```html
<input min="1" max="5" class="out-of-range:border-red-500 ..." />
```

### Apply Hover Styles with Tailwind CSS Utility Classes

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/styling-with-utility-classes

This example demonstrates how to apply styles to an element on hover using Tailwind CSS utility classes. By prefixing a utility like `bg-sky-700` with `hover:`, the background color changes only when the button is hovered over, showcasing Tailwind's variant system for interactive states.

```html
<button class="bg-sky-500 hover:bg-sky-700 ...">Save changes</button>
```

### Update placeholder color styling in Tailwind CSS v4 Preflight

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

In v4, placeholder text uses current text color at 50% opacity instead of gray-400. Add this CSS to your base layer to preserve v3 behavior with the gray-400 color for input and textarea placeholders.

```css
@layer base {
  input::placeholder,
  textarea::placeholder {
    color: var(--color-gray-400);
  }
}
```

---

### Apply mask-clip utilities in HTML with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-clip

Use mask-clip utility classes to control the bounding box of an element's mask. The example demonstrates three different mask-clip values (border, padding, content) applied to div elements with custom mask images and background images. Responsive variants like md: can be used to apply utilities at specific breakpoints.

```html
<div
  class="mask-clip-border border-3 p-1.5 mask-[url(/img/circle.png)] bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)] ..."
></div>
<div
  class="mask-clip-padding border-3 p-1.5 mask-[url(/img/circle.png)] bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)] ..."
></div>
<div
  class="mask-clip-content border-3 p-1.5 mask-[url(/img/circle.png)] bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)] ..."
></div>
```

### Using @apply and Theme Variables in Vue/Svelte/CSS Modules with Tailwind CSS v4

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Stylesheets bundled separately (e.g., Vue `<style>` blocks, Svelte, CSS modules) in Tailwind CSS v4 do not automatically access global theme variables or custom utilities. This snippet provides two solutions: using `@reference` to import definitions without duplicating CSS, or directly applying CSS theme variables for improved performance and simpler styling.

```vue
<template><h1>Hello world!</h1></template>
<style>
@reference "../../app.css";
h1 {
  @apply text-2xl font-bold text-red-500;
}
</style>
```

```vue
<template><h1>Hello world!</h1></template>
<style>
h1 {
  color: var(--text-red-500);
}
</style>
```

---

### Apply Border Start Color with Red Palette in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/border-color

Utility classes for setting inline-start border color using the red color palette. The border-s-red-\* classes apply the border-inline-start-color CSS property with predefined red shades from 50 to 400, each with corresponding OKLCH color values for consistent red tone rendering.

```css
/* border-s-red-50 */
border-inline-start-color: var(--color-red-50); /* oklch(97.1% 0.013 17.38) */

/* border-s-red-100 */
border-inline-start-color: var(--color-red-100); /* oklch(93.6% 0.032 17.717) */

/* border-s-red-200 */
border-inline-start-color: var(--color-red-200); /* oklch(88.5% 0.062 18.334) */

/* border-s-red-300 */
border-inline-start-color: var(--color-red-300); /* oklch(80.8% 0.114 19.571) */

/* border-s-red-400 */
```

```html
<div class="mask-add md:mask-subtract ..."><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Enable Arbitrary Utility Values with Type Validation in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/adding-custom-styles

This example demonstrates the `--value([{type}])` syntax (with square brackets) for supporting arbitrary values in Tailwind CSS utilities. It allows users to define custom values like `tab-[1]` while enforcing type validation, ensuring the arbitrary input conforms to a specified data type such as `integer`.

```css
@utility tab-* {
  tab-size: --value([integer]);
}
```

### Apply Text Color on Hover with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/color

This example shows how to change text color when a user hovers over an element using Tailwind CSS hover variants. It applies different hover colors for light and dark modes, enhancing interactivity and user feedback.

```html
<p class="...">
  Oh I gotta get on that
  <a
    class="underline hover:text-blue-600 dark:hover:text-blue-400"
    href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet"
    >internet</a
  >, I'm late on everything!
</p>
```

### Apply mask-luminance utility with gradient mask in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-mode

Demonstrates using the mask-luminance utility where the luminance value of the mask determines visibility. The example uses grayscale colors (white to black) with radial gradient mask utilities for predictable results. Luminance-based masking works best with grayscale color values.

```html
<div
  class="mask-luminance mask-r-from-white mask-r-from-50% mask-r-to-black bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)] ..."
></div>
```

### Example Default Tailwind CSS Theme Variables

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/theme

This CSS code block illustrates how default theme variables for fonts, colors, and shadows are defined within the `theme.css` file using CSS custom properties inside an `@theme` block. These variables drive the out-of-the-box utility classes provided by Tailwind CSS.

```css
@theme {
  --font-sans:
    ui-sans-serif, system-ui, sans-serif, "Apple Color Emoji", "Segoe UI Emoji",
    "Segoe UI Symbol", "Noto Color Emoji";
  --font-serif: ui-serif, Georgia, Cambria, "Times New Roman", Times, serif;
  --font-mono:
    ui-monospace, SFMono-Regular, Menlo, Monaco, Consolas, "Liberation Mono",
    "Courier New", monospace;
  --color-red-50: oklch(0.971 0.013 17.38);
  --color-red-100: oklch(0.936 0.032 17.717);
  --color-red-200: oklch(0.885 0.062 18.334); /* ... */
  --shadow-2xs: 0 1px rgb(0 0 0 / 0.05);
  --shadow-xs: 0 1px 2px 0 rgb(0 0 0 / 0.05);
  --shadow-sm:
    0 1px 3px 0 rgb(0 0 0 / 0.1), 0 1px 2px -1px rgb(0 0 0 / 0.1); /* ... */
}
```

### Style HTML <details> element based on open state with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This snippet shows how to use the `open:` variant in Tailwind CSS to apply styles conditionally when an HTML `<details>` element is in its open state. For example, `open:border-black/10` applies a border when the details element is expanded.

```HTML
<details class="border border-transparent open:border-black/10 open:bg-gray-100 ..." open>  <summary class="text-sm leading-6 font-semibold text-gray-900 select-none">Why do they call it Ovaltine?</summary>  <div class="mt-3 text-sm leading-6 text-gray-600">    <p>The mug is round. The jar is round. They should call it Roundtine.</p>  </div></details>
```

### Alternative to Tailwind CSS ::before Pseudo-element with a Span

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This HTML snippet provides an alternative to using the `::before` pseudo-element for decorative styling by employing a regular `<span>` element. It achieves the same visual effect (a skewed background) as the pseudo-element example but is often considered more readable and simpler to implement, especially when the content is not purely decorative.

```html
<blockquote class="text-center text-2xl font-semibold text-gray-900 italic">
  When you look
  <span class="relative">
    <span
      class="absolute -inset-1 block -skew-y-3 bg-pink-500"
      aria-hidden="true"
    ></span>
    <span class="relative text-white">annoyed</span>
  </span>
  all the time, people think that you're busy.
</blockquote>
```

---

### Apply nth-last-of-type styles with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

Style an element at a specific position from the end, of the same type, using the `nth-last-of-type` variant. This example uses `nth-last-of-type-3` and `nth-last-of-type-[3n+1]` to apply horizontal margins to `a` tags based on their position among `a` siblings, counting from the end.

```html
<nav>
  <img src="/logo.svg" alt="Vandelay Industries" /> {#each links as link}
  <a
    href="#"
    class="mx-2 nth-last-of-type-3:mx-6 nth-last-of-type-[3n+1]:mx-7 ..."
  >
    <!-- ... -->
  </a>
  {/each} <button>More</button>
</nav>
```

---

### Apply single-side padding with Tailwind CSS `pt/pr/pb/pl-<number>` utilities

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/padding

Illustrates how to apply padding to individual sides of an element using specific utilities such as `pt-6` (top), `pr-4` (right), `pb-8` (bottom), and `pl-2` (left). Each utility targets a single direction for precise control over spacing.

```html
<div class="pt-6 ...">pt-6</div>
<div class="pr-4 ...">pr-4</div>
<div class="pb-8 ...">pb-8</div>
<div class="pl-2 ...">pl-2</div>
```

---

### Update Tailwind CSS Ring Utility Default Width (v3 to v4)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Describes the change in Tailwind CSS v4 where the default `ring` width is now `1px` instead of `3px`, aligning it with borders and outlines. To maintain the v3 behavior of a `3px` ring, users should explicitly use `ring-3`.

```html
<input class="ring ring-blue-500" /><input class="ring-3 ring-blue-500" />
```

---

### Tailwind CSS backdrop-sepia utility class reference

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/backdrop-filter-sepia

Complete reference of available backdrop-sepia utility classes and their corresponding CSS output. Includes standard classes, numbered variants, custom property syntax, and arbitrary value bracket notation.

```css
/* backdrop-sepia */
backdrop-filter: sepia(100%);

/* backdrop-sepia-<number> */
backdrop-filter: sepia(<number>%);

/* backdrop-sepia-(<custom-property>) */
backdrop-filter: sepia(var(<custom-property>));

/* backdrop-sepia-[<value>] */
backdrop-filter: sepia(<value>);
```

```html
<button class="ring-2 ring-blue-500 ...">Subscribe</button>
<button class="ring-2 ring-blue-500/50 ...">Subscribe</button>
```

### Customize Tailwind CSS Theme Colors

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/color

This example illustrates how to extend the Tailwind CSS theme with custom colors using the `@theme` directive. It defines a new color variable, `regal-blue`, which can then be used as a standard Tailwind utility class in HTML, providing a consistent branding experience.

```css
@theme {
  --color-regal-blue: #243c5a;
}
```

```html
<p class="text-regal-blue">Lorem ipsum dolor sit amet...</p>
```

```html
<div class="from-regal-blue"><!-- ... --></div>
```

---

### Register custom utilities with @utility API in Tailwind CSS v4

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

In v4, use the `@utility` API instead of `@layer utilities` to register custom utilities that work with variants. Custom utilities are sorted by property count, allowing component utilities to be overridden by Tailwind utilities without additional configuration.

```css
@layer utilities {
  .tab-4 {
    tab-size: 4;
  }
}

@utility tab-4 {
  tab-size: 4;
}
```

---

### Preserve Tailwind CSS v3 ring behavior with theme variables

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Add custom theme variables to your CSS to maintain v3 ring defaults (3px width and blue-500 color). This approach is supported for compatibility but is not considered idiomatic usage in Tailwind CSS v4.0.

```css
@theme {
  --default-ring-width: 3px;
  --default-ring-color: var(--color-blue-500);
}
```

---

### Customize Breakpoints with Theme Variables

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

Use --breakpoint-\* CSS custom properties in the @theme block to customize existing breakpoints or create new ones. All breakpoints should use the same unit (rem is recommended) to ensure proper sorting and prevent unexpected overrides.

```css
@import "tailwindcss";
@theme {
  --breakpoint-xs: 30rem;
  --breakpoint-2xl: 100rem;
  --breakpoint-3xl: 120rem;
}
```

### Safelisting Specific Tailwind CSS Utilities with @source inline()

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/detecting-classes-in-source-files

This example illustrates how to force Tailwind CSS to generate specific utility classes that might not be detected in your content files. Using `@source inline("className")`, you can ensure a particular class, like `underline`, is always included in the final CSS output.

```CSS
@import "tailwindcss";@source inline("underline");
```

```CSS
.underline {  text-decoration-line: underline;}
```

The class `brightness-(--my-brightness)` dynamically applies the brightness value defined by the `--my-brightness` CSS variable, providing flexibility for theme-based or dynamic adjustments.

```html
<img class="brightness-(--my-brightness) ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
```

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example illustrates how to use the `motion-reduce` variant to conditionally hide or disable animations when the user has requested reduced motion via the `prefers-reduced-motion` media query. It's useful for improving accessibility by minimizing non-essential motion.

```html
<button type="button" class="bg-indigo-500 ..." disabled>

    <!-- ... -->
  </svg>

</button>
```

### Prevent text wrapping with Tailwind CSS `whitespace-nowrap`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/white-space

This example shows how to use the `whitespace-nowrap` utility class in Tailwind CSS to prevent text from wrapping within an HTML element. Newlines and multiple spaces will be collapsed, and content might overflow its container if not explicitly handled by other styles like `overflow-auto`.

```html
<p class="overflow-auto whitespace-nowrap">
  Hey everyone!It's almost 2022 and we still don't know if there are aliens
  living among us, or do we? Maybe the person writing this is an alien.You will
  never know.
</p>
```

---

### Update Variant Stacking Order - HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Reverse the order of stacked variants when migrating to Tailwind CSS v4, as variants now apply left to right instead of right to left. This primarily affects direct child variants (\*) and typography plugin variants (prose-headings) when stacked with other variants.

```html
<ul class="py-4 first:*:pt-0 last:*:pb-0">
  <li>One</li>
  <li>Two</li>
  <li>Three</li>
</ul>
```

---

### Understand Tailwind CSS `space-x/y` Selector Change (v4 CSS)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Explains the performance-driven change in the CSS selector used by `space-x-*` and `space-y-*` utilities in Tailwind CSS v4. The new selector targets `:not(:last-child)` instead of `:not([hidden]) ~ :not([hidden])` to improve performance on large pages.

```css
/* Before */
.space-y-4 > :not([hidden]) ~ :not([hidden]) {
  margin-top: 1rem;
}
/* Now */
.space-y-4 > :not(:last-child) {
  margin-bottom: 1rem;
}
```

### Resolve Bare Utility Values with Specific Data Types in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/adding-custom-styles

This example illustrates using the `--value({type})` syntax in a Tailwind CSS `@utility` rule to resolve bare numeric values, validating them against a specified data type like `integer`. This allows for the creation of utilities such as `tab-1` or `tab-76`, ensuring the value conforms to the expected type.

```css
@utility tab-* {
  tab-size: --value(integer);
}
```

### Style form inputs with Tailwind CSS `disabled` and `invalid` variants

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example illustrates how to apply styles to form input elements based on their `disabled` or `invalid` states using Tailwind CSS variants. This approach reduces conditional logic in templates by letting the browser manage state-based styling, applying different borders, text colors, and backgrounds for various input states.

```html
<input
  type="text"
  value="tbone"
  disabled
  class="invalid:border-pink-500 invalid:text-pink-600 focus:border-sky-500 focus:outline focus:outline-sky-500 focus:invalid:border-pink-500 focus:invalid:outline-pink-500 disabled:border-gray-200 disabled:bg-gray-50 disabled:text-gray-500 disabled:shadow-none dark:disabled:border-gray-700 dark:disabled:bg-gray-800/20 ..."
/>
```

### Control Element Flow with Block and Inline Display in HTML/CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/display

This snippet demonstrates how to use Tailwind CSS's `inline`, `inline-block`, and `block` utilities to control the flow of text and elements within a document. These utilities directly map to the CSS `display` property, affecting how elements wrap and occupy space. The example shows how `inline` allows text to wrap normally, `inline-block` wraps the element to prevent overflow, and `block` places the element on its own line.

```html
<p>
  When controlling the flow of text, using the CSS property
  <span class="inline">display: inline</span> will cause the text inside the
  element to wrap normally.
</p>
<p>
  While using the property
  <span class="inline-block">display: inline-block</span> will wrap the element
  to prevent the text inside from extending beyond its parent.
</p>
<p>
  Lastly, using the property <span class="block">display: block</span> will put
  the element on its own line and fill its parent.
</p>
```

### Apply Tailwind CSS styles for RTL/LTR layouts

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This snippet demonstrates using `rtl:` and `ltr:` variants in Tailwind CSS to apply directional styles for multi-directional layouts. For example, `ltr:ml-3 rtl:mr-3` ensures correct spacing whether the layout is left-to-right or right-to-left. These variants are useful for internationalized applications.

```HTML
<div class="group flex items-center">  <img class="h-12 w-12 shrink-0 rounded-full" src="..." alt="" />  <div class="ltr:ml-3 rtl:mr-3">    <p class="text-gray-700 group-hover:text-gray-900 ...">...</p>    <p class="text-gray-500 group-hover:text-gray-700 ...">...</p>  </div></div>
```

### Apply Tailwind CSS styles based on data attribute presence

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This snippet demonstrates how to apply Tailwind CSS styles based on the mere presence of a data attribute using `data-*` variants. For example, `data-active:border-purple-500` applies a border color if the `data-active` attribute exists on the element.

```HTML
<!-- Will apply --><div data-active class="border border-gray-300 data-active:border-purple-500">  <!-- ... --></div><!-- Will not apply --><div class="border border-gray-300 data-active:border-purple-500">  <!-- ... --></div>
```

---

### Tailwind CSS `*` Variant Override Limitation Example

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This snippet highlights a limitation when using the `*` variant: styles applied from a parent using `*` cannot be overridden by utility classes directly on the child element. This is due to the order of CSS rule generation and specificity, where child rules are generated after parent rules with the same specificity.

```html
<ul class="*:bg-sky-50 ...">
  <li class="bg-red-50 ...">Sales</li>
  <li>Marketing</li>
  <li>SEO</li>
  <!-- ... -->
</ul>
```

---

### Control Border Color Opacity in HTML with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/border-color

This HTML example illustrates how to modify the opacity of border colors using Tailwind CSS's color opacity modifiers. By appending `/100`, `/75`, or `/50` to a color utility like `border-indigo-500`, developers can control the transparency of the border. This allows for subtle visual effects and better integration with varying backgrounds.

```html
<div class="border-4 border-indigo-500/100"></div>
<div class="border-4 border-indigo-500/75"></div>
<div class="border-4 border-indigo-500/50"></div>
```

---

### Understand Tailwind CSS `divide-x/y` Selector Change (v4 CSS)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Explains the performance-driven change in the CSS selector used by `divide-x-*` and `divide-y-*` utilities in Tailwind CSS v4. The new selector targets `:not(:last-child)` instead of `:not([hidden]) ~ :not([hidden])` to address performance issues on large pages.

```css
/* Before */
.divide-y-4 > :not([hidden]) ~ :not([hidden]) {
  border-top-width: 4px;
}
/* Now */
.divide-y-4 > :not(:last-child) {
  border-bottom-width: 4px;
}
```

---

### Use Logical Properties for Directional Positioning in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/top-right-bottom-left

Demonstrates using start-<number> and end-<number> utilities for logical positioning that adapts to text direction. Automatically maps to left/right based on whether the document is left-to-right (LTR) or right-to-left (RTL).

```HTML
<div dir="ltr">
  <div class="relative size-32 ...">
    <div class="absolute start-0 top-0 size-14 ..."></div>
  </div>
  <div>
    <div dir="rtl">
      <div class="relative size-32 ...">
        <div class="absolute start-0 top-0 size-14 ..."></div>
      </div>
      <div></div>
    </div>
  </div>
</div>
```

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Explains that Tailwind CSS v4 changed the default border color for `border-*` and `divide-*` utilities from `gray-200` to `currentColor`. Users must now explicitly specify a color, such as `border-gray-200`, where these utilities are used.

```html
<div class="border border-gray-200 px-2 py-3 ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

---

### Migrate Tailwind CSS `outline-none` to `outline-hidden` (v3 to v4)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Explains the renaming of `outline-none` to `outline-hidden` in Tailwind CSS v4 for improved accessibility clarity, as the old `outline-none` still showed in forced colors mode. A new `outline-none` utility now truly sets `outline-style: none`. Users should replace `outline-none` with `outline-hidden` for the previous behavior.

```html
<input class="focus:outline-none" /><input class="focus:outline-hidden" />
```

---

### Create Phantom Container with Contents Utility

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/display

Use the `contents` utility to create a phantom container whose children act as direct children of the parent element. This is useful for flattening the DOM hierarchy without affecting layout. The children inherit flex properties from the parent container.

```html
<div class="flex ...">
  <div class="flex-1 ...">01</div>
  <div class="contents">
    <div class="flex-1 ...">02</div>
    <div class="flex-1 ...">03</div>
  </div>
  <div class="flex-1 ...">04</div>
</div>
```

---

### Background Color CSS Variable Mappings

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/background-color

Tailwind background color utilities map to CSS custom properties with OKLCH color space values. Examples include `bg-gray-900` mapping to `--color-gray-900` with oklch(21% 0.034 264.665), providing consistent color scales across gray, zinc, neutral, and stone palettes.

```css
background-color: var(--color-gray-900); /* oklch(21% 0.034 264.665) */
background-color: var(--color-zinc-500); /* oklch(55.2% 0.016 285.938) */
background-color: var(--color-neutral-600); /* oklch(43.9% 0 0) */
background-color: var(--color-stone-400); /* oklch(70.9% 0.01 56.259) */
```

```html
<div class="perspective-[750px] ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

---

### Incorrect Tailwind CSS peer Usage: Styling Non-Previous Siblings

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example illustrates an incorrect usage of the Tailwind CSS `peer` variant. The `peer` class must be applied to a _previous_ sibling for the `peer-*` variants to work correctly due to CSS subsequent-sibling combinator limitations. Here, `peer-invalid:text-red-500` is applied to a `<span>` that is not a subsequent sibling of the `input` with `peer`.

```html
<label>
  <span class="peer-invalid:text-red-500 ...">Email</span>
  <input type="email" class="peer ..."
/></label>
```

---

### Tailwind CSS Text Shadow Color Utility Class Examples

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/text-shadow

This snippet illustrates the pattern of Tailwind CSS utility classes for setting text shadow colors. Each class, following the `text-shadow-[color]-[shade]` convention, translates into a CSS custom property `--tw-text-shadow-color` that references a specific color variable from the Tailwind theme. This mechanism allows for easy and consistent application of text shadow colors across a project.

```css
--tw-text-shadow-color var(--color-yellow-100);
```

```css
--tw-text-shadow-color var(--color-lime-500);
```

```css
--tw-text-shadow-color var(--color-green-950);
```

```css
--tw-text-shadow-color var(--color-emerald-400);
```

```css
--tw-text-shadow-color var(--color-teal-100);
```

### Apply Responsive Maximum Width with Tailwind CSS Breakpoint Variants

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/max-width

Demonstrates how to use breakpoint variants (e.g., `md:`) to apply `max-width` utilities only at specific screen sizes and above. This enables responsive design, adjusting element widths based on viewport dimensions.

```html
<div class="max-w-sm md:max-w-lg ..."><!-- ... --></div>
```
