---

### Use CSS Variables Instead of theme() Function - CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Prefer CSS variables over the theme() function for accessing theme values in Tailwind CSS v4. Use the CSS variable name syntax (--color-red-500) instead of dot notation for theme() when variables are not supported, such as in media queries.

```css
.my-class {
  background-color: var(--color-red-500);
}
```

```css
@media (width >= theme(--breakpoint-xl)) {
  /* ... */
}
```

---

### Apply all-side padding with Tailwind CSS `p-<number>` utility

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/padding

Demonstrates how to use `p-<number>` utilities like `p-4` and `p-8` to apply padding uniformly to all sides of an HTML element. This is a common way to add consistent spacing around content.

```html
<div class="p-8 ...">p-8</div>
```

---

### Disable Clears with Tailwind CSS `clear-none` Utility

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/clear

This snippet demonstrates how to use the `clear-none` utility in Tailwind CSS to reset any previously applied clear styles on an element. It ensures that the element will not be affected by floating elements, allowing content to flow naturally. The example shows `clear-none` applied to a paragraph following floated images.

```html
<article>
  <img class="float-left ..." src="/img/green-mountains.jpg" />
  <img class="float-right ..." src="/img/snow-mountains.jpg" />
  <p class="clear-none ...">Maybe we can live without libraries...</p>
</article>
```

---

### Span Columns with Tailwind CSS `col-span-<number>`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/grid-column

Demonstrates how to use `col-span-<number>` utilities in Tailwind CSS to make an element span a specific number of grid columns. This example shows elements spanning 2 and 4 columns within a 3-column grid layout, illustrating basic column spanning functionality.

```html
<div class="grid grid-cols-3 gap-4">
  <div class="...">01</div>
  <div class="...">02</div>
  <div class="...">03</div>
  <div class="col-span-2 ...">04</div>
  <div class="...">05</div>
  <div class="...">06</div>
  <div class="col-span-2 ...">07</div>
</div>
```

---

### Apply bg-cover utility for filling container

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/background-size

Use the bg-cover class to scale the background image until it fills the background layer, cropping the image if necessary. This is useful when you want the background to completely cover the container.

```html
<div class="bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)] bg-cover bg-center"></div>
```

### Apply Custom Value Maximum Height with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/max-height

This HTML snippet demonstrates how to apply a completely custom maximum height value using Tailwind CSS's arbitrary value syntax, `max-h-[<value>]`. This allows developers to specify any valid CSS height unit directly within the utility class. The example sets a maximum height of `220px`.

```html
<div class="max-h-[220px] ..."><!-- ... --></div>
```

---

### Apply custom padding with Tailwind CSS variable shorthand `p-(<custom-property>)`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/padding

Demonstrates the shorthand syntax `p-(<custom-property>)` for applying padding using CSS variables. This automatically wraps the custom property in `var()`, simplifying the use of dynamic padding values defined elsewhere in your CSS.

```html
<div class="p-(--my-padding) ..."><!-- ... --></div>
```

---

### Utilize Tailwind CSS Theme Variables in Arbitrary HTML Values

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/theme

Illustrates the use of Tailwind CSS theme variables within arbitrary values in HTML, particularly in conjunction with CSS functions like `calc()`. This example shows how to create a concentric border radius by subtracting a pixel from a theme variable (`--radius-xl`) for a nested inset element, providing precise control over styling.

```html
<div class="relative rounded-xl">
  <div class="absolute inset-px rounded-[calc(var(--radius-xl)-1px)]">
    <!-- ... -->
  </div>
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

---

### Restore cursor pointer on buttons in Tailwind CSS v4

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Buttons now use `cursor: default` instead of `cursor: pointer` to match browser defaults. Add this CSS to your base layer to restore the v3 behavior of showing pointer cursor on enabled buttons and elements with role="button".

```css
@layer base {
  button:not(:disabled),
  [role="button"]:not(:disabled) {
    cursor: pointer;
  }
}
```

---

### Apply box-decoration-break utilities in HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/box-decoration-break

Use box-decoration-slice and box-decoration-clone classes to control how element fragments render across multiple lines. The slice value renders as distinct blocks while clone renders as continuous fragments. Supports responsive design with breakpoint prefixes like md:.

```html
<span
  class="box-decoration-slice bg-linear-to-r from-indigo-600 to-pink-500 px-2 text-white ..."
>
  Hello<br />
  World
</span>
<span
  class="box-decoration-clone bg-linear-to-r from-indigo-600 to-pink-500 px-2 text-white ..."
>
  Hello<br />
  World
</span>
```

### Set Maximum Width using Tailwind CSS Container Scale Utilities

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/max-width

Shows how to apply maximum widths based on Tailwind's predefined container scale (e.g., `max-w-md`, `max-w-xl`). These utilities are ideal for aligning content with common screen size breakpoints.

```html
<div class="max-w-md ..."><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Utilize Tailwind CSS `nth-*` and `nth-last-*` variants for positional styling

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This snippet demonstrates the use of `nth-*` and `nth-last-*` variants in Tailwind CSS to apply styles based on an element's position among its siblings or siblings of the same type. It shows examples like `nth-3:underline` and `nth-last-of-type-6:underline`, and notes support for arbitrary values and complex expressions.

```html
<div class="nth-3:underline"><!-- ... --></div>
<div class="nth-last-5:underline"><!-- ... --></div>
<div class="nth-of-type-4:underline"><!-- ... --></div>
<div class="nth-last-of-type-6:underline"><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Apply contrast filter using CSS custom property in HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/filter-contrast

Use the contrast-(<custom-property>) syntax as shorthand for contrast-[var(<custom-property>)] to apply contrast values from CSS custom properties. The var() function is automatically added by Tailwind CSS.

```html
<img class="contrast-(--my-contrast) ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
```

### Apply text-balance utility in HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/text-wrap

Use the text-balance class to distribute text evenly across each line, creating more balanced line lengths. Best suited for headings and limited to blocks of approximately 6 lines or less due to browser performance constraints.

```html
<article>
  <h3 class="text-balance">Beloved Manhattan soup stand closes</h3>
  <p>New Yorkers are facing the winter chill...</p>
</article>
```

### Apply responsive text decoration styles with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/text-decoration-style

This snippet illustrates how to apply text decoration styles conditionally based on screen size using Tailwind CSS responsive variants. The `md:` prefix ensures the `decoration-dashed` utility is applied only for medium screens and above, allowing for adaptive designs.

```html
<p class="underline md:decoration-dashed ...">Lorem ipsum dolor sit amet...</p>
```

---

### Restore Tailwind CSS v3 Default Border Color with CSS (v4 CSS)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Provides a CSS solution to restore the Tailwind CSS v3 default border color behavior (`gray-200`) for `border-*` and `divide-*` utilities in v4. This is achieved by adding a `@layer base` rule to set `border-color` using a CSS variable fallback.

```css
@layer base {
  *,
  ::after,
  ::before,
  ::backdrop,
  ::file-selector-button {
    border-color: var(--color-gray-200, currentColor);
  }
}
```

---

### Using custom @supports variants in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This snippet demonstrates how to apply styles using a custom `@supports` variant that has been previously defined in the Tailwind CSS configuration. This simplifies the application of complex `@supports` rules in HTML.

```html
<div class="supports-grid:grid">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

---

### Responsive object-position Design - Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/object-position

Illustrates responsive design with object-position utilities using Tailwind CSS breakpoint variants. The md: prefix applies the object-top class only at medium screen sizes and above, while defaulting to object-center on smaller screens.

```html
<img class="object-center md:object-top ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
```

### Implement Responsive Text Color Design

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/text-color

Use breakpoint variants like `md:` to apply different text colors at specific screen sizes. Enables mobile-first responsive color strategies.

```html
<p class="text-blue-600 md:text-green-600">Lorem ipsum dolor sit amet...</p>
```

### Apply Percentage-Based Maximum Width with Tailwind CSS `max-w-<fraction>` Utilities

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/max-width

Illustrates the use of Tailwind CSS `max-w-full` or `max-w-<fraction>` utilities to set an element's maximum width as a percentage of its parent. This is useful for creating fluid layouts that adapt to available space.

```html
<div class="w-full max-w-9/10 ...">max-w-9/10</div>
<div class="w-full max-w-3/4 ...">max-w-3/4</div>
<div class="w-full max-w-1/2 ...">max-w-1/2</div>
<div class="w-full max-w-1/3 ...">max-w-1/3</div>
```

### Accessing Tailwind CSS Theme Values in JavaScript

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/upgrade-guide

Tailwind CSS v4 encourages using direct CSS variables for theme values in JavaScript, replacing the `resolveConfig` function from v3. This snippet shows how to use a CSS variable for `backgroundColor` in a JSX component (e.g., with Motion library) and how to retrieve a resolved CSS variable value like `--shadow-xl` using `getComputedStyle` in plain JavaScript.

```jsx
<motion.div animate={{ backgroundColor: "var(--color-blue-500)" }} />
```

```javascript
let styles = getComputedStyle(document.documentElement);
let shadow = styles.getPropertyValue("--shadow-xl");
```

---

### Apply responsive grid-auto-rows utilities in HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/grid-auto-rows

This snippet demonstrates how to apply `grid-auto-rows` utilities responsively using Tailwind CSS breakpoint variants. The `md:auto-rows-min` class ensures that implicit grid rows have a minimum content size on medium screens and above, overriding the default `auto-rows-max`.

```html
<div class="grid grid-flow-row auto-rows-max md:auto-rows-min ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Apply Custom Grayscale Values in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/filter-grayscale

Shows how to use arbitrary values with the `grayscale-[<value>]` syntax. This allows setting a precise grayscale level not covered by predefined utilities, such as `grayscale-[0.5]` for 50% grayscale.

```html
<img class="grayscale-[0.5] ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
```

---

### Style elements based on descendant state using Tailwind CSS `group-has-*` variant

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This example demonstrates how to use the `group-has-*` variant in Tailwind CSS to style an element within a `group` based on the presence or state of a descendant. Specifically, it shows how to conditionally display an SVG icon if a link (`a`) is present within the parent `div` marked with the `group` class.

```html
<div class="group ...">
  <img src="..." />
  <h4>Spencer Sharp</h4>
  <svg class="hidden group-has-[a]:block ..."><!-- ... --></svg>
  <p>Product Designer at <a href="...">planeteria.tech</a></p>
</div>
```

---

### Apply custom container query variant in HTML markup

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

Use the custom container variant in your HTML to create responsive layouts based on container width. The `@8xl:flex-row` class applies flex-row styling when the container reaches the 8xl breakpoint.

```html
<div class="@container">
  <div class="flex flex-col @8xl:flex-row">
    <!-- ... -->
  </div>
</div>
```

---

### Apply flex-wrap utilities responsively with breakpoint variants

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/flex-wrap

Prefix a flex-wrap utility with a breakpoint variant like md: to apply the utility only at medium screen sizes and above. This enables different flex wrapping behavior across different device sizes.

```html
<div class="flex flex-wrap md:flex-wrap-reverse ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

---

### Prefix Tailwind CSS Utility Classes

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/styling-with-utility-classes

This snippet illustrates how to use the `prefix` option when importing Tailwind CSS in `app.css`. By specifying a prefix like `tw`, all generated Tailwind utility classes and CSS variables will be prepended with `tw:`, preventing conflicts with existing class names in a project. The compiled CSS demonstrates how a class like `text-red-500` becomes `tw:text-red-500`.

```css
@import "tailwindcss" prefix(tw);
```

```css
@layer theme {
  :root {
    --tw-color-red-500: oklch(0.637 0.237 25.331);
  }
}
@layer utilities {
  .tw\:text-red-500 {
    color: var(--tw-color-red-500);
  }
}
```

---

### Custom Animation with CSS Variables

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/animation

Demonstrates using the `animate-(<custom-property>)` syntax to reference custom CSS variables for animations. This is shorthand for `animate-[var(<custom-property>)]` and automatically wraps the variable in the `var()` function.

```html
<div class="animate-(--my-animation) ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Apply `theme()` to Tailwind CSS Theme Import (CSS)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/preflight

Illustrates how to use `theme(static)` or `theme(inline)` with the `tailwindcss/theme.css` import. These functions control how theme variables are generated, allowing for static or inline variable output.

```css
@layer theme, base, components, utilities;
@import "tailwindcss/theme.css" layer(theme);
@import "tailwindcss/theme.css" layer(theme) theme(static);
@import "tailwindcss/utilities.css" layer(utilities);
```

### Get Resolved Tailwind CSS Theme Variable Values in JavaScript

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/theme

Explains how to programmatically retrieve the computed, resolved value of a CSS variable (representing a Tailwind CSS theme variable) in JavaScript. It uses `getComputedStyle(document.documentElement)` and `getPropertyValue()` to access values like `--shadow-xl` from the document root, enabling dynamic logic based on current theme values.

```javascript
let styles = getComputedStyle(document.documentElement);
let shadow = styles.getPropertyValue("--shadow-xl");
```

---

### Statically positioning elements with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/position

Demonstrates how to use the `static` utility class in Tailwind CSS to position an element according to the normal document flow. With statically positioned elements, any offsets will be ignored, and the element will not act as a position reference for absolutely positioned children.

```html
<div class="static ...">
  <p>Static parent</p>
  <div class="absolute bottom-0 left-0 ..."><p>Absolute child</p></div>
</div>
```

---

### Combine Theme, Bare, and Arbitrary Values in Tailwind CSS Utilities

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/adding-custom-styles

This code illustrates how to combine theme-based, bare, and arbitrary value resolution within a single Tailwind CSS `@utility` rule using multiple `--value()` declarations. Declarations that fail to resolve are automatically omitted from the output, providing flexible and robust value handling for utilities like `tab-*`.

```css
@theme {
  --tab-size-github: 8;
}
@utility tab-* {
  tab-size: --value([integer]);
  tab-size: --value(integer);
  tab-size: --value(--tab-size-*);
}
```

---

### Allowing Flex Items to Grow with Tailwind CSS `grow`

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/flex-grow

Demonstrates the `grow` utility in Tailwind CSS, enabling a flex item to expand and fill available space within its container. This is useful for distributing remaining space among flexible elements.

```html
<div class="flex ...">
  <div class="size-14 flex-none ...">01</div>
  <div class="size-14 grow ...">02</div>
  <div class="size-14 flex-none ...">03</div>
</div>
```

### Apply Responsive Styles with Tailwind CSS Breakpoints

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/styling-with-utility-classes

This snippet illustrates how to implement responsive designs using Tailwind CSS breakpoint prefixes. By adding `sm:` to a utility like `grid-cols-3`, the layout dynamically adjusts to a 3-column grid only on screens at or above the small (`sm`) breakpoint.

```html
<div class="grid grid-cols-2 sm:grid-cols-3"><!-- ... --></div>
```

### Set custom aspect ratio using arbitrary values or CSS variables in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/aspect-ratio

Illustrates two methods for defining custom aspect ratios. The first uses arbitrary value syntax `aspect-[<value>]` for direct calculations, while the second uses `aspect-(<custom-property>)` to reference a CSS variable.

```html
<img class="aspect-[calc(4*3+1)/3] ..." src="/img/villas.jpg" />
```

```html
<img class="aspect-(--my-aspect-ratio) ..." src="/img/villas.jpg" />
```

### Create Table Layout with Table Display Utilities

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/display

Use table display utilities (`table`, `table-row`, `table-cell`, `table-header-group`, `table-row-group`) to create elements that behave like their respective HTML table elements. This allows semantic table layouts using div elements with Tailwind CSS classes.

```html
<div class="table w-full ...">
  <div class="table-header-group ...">
    <div class="table-row">
      <div class="table-cell text-left ...">Song</div>
      <div class="table-cell text-left ...">Artist</div>
      <div class="table-cell text-left ...">Year</div>
    </div>
  </div>
  <div class="table-row-group">
    <div class="table-row">
      <div class="table-cell ...">
        The Sliding Mr. Bones (Next Stop, Pottersville)
      </div>
      <div class="table-cell ...">Malcolm Lockyer</div>
      <div class="table-cell ...">1961</div>
    </div>
    <div class="table-row">
      <div class="table-cell ...">Witchy Woman</div>
      <div class="table-cell ...">The Eagles</div>
      <div class="table-cell ...">1972</div>
    </div>
    <div class="table-row">
      <div class="table-cell ...">Shining Star</div>
      <div class="table-cell ...">Earth, Wind, and Fire</div>
      <div class="table-cell ...">1975</div>
    </div>
  </div>
</div>
```

### Create Responsive Profile Card with Hover States

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/styling-with-utility-classes

A fully responsive profile component with conditional layout changes using sm: responsive variants. Includes hover and active state styling on button elements, demonstrating how Tailwind enables interactive states that inline styles cannot achieve. Adapts from vertical to horizontal layout on larger screens.

```html
<div
  class="flex flex-col gap-2 p-8 sm:flex-row sm:items-center sm:gap-6 sm:py-4 ..."
>
  <img
    class="mx-auto block h-24 rounded-full sm:mx-0 sm:shrink-0"
    src="/img/erin-lindford.jpg"
    alt=""
  />
  <div class="space-y-2 text-center sm:text-left">
    <div class="space-y-0.5">
      <p class="text-lg font-semibold text-black">Erin Lindford</p>
      <p class="font-medium text-gray-500">Product Engineer</p>
    </div>
    <button
      class="border-purple-200 text-purple-600 hover:border-transparent hover:bg-purple-600 hover:text-white active:bg-purple-700 ..."
    >
      Message
    </button>
  </div>
</div>
```

### Generate spacing values with --spacing() function

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/functions-and-directives

Use the --spacing() function to generate spacing values based on your theme configuration. This function multiplies the spacing unit by the provided factor and compiles to calc() expressions.

```CSS
.my-element {
  margin: --spacing(4);
}
```

---

### Tailwind CSS `inset` Utilities for All Sides

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/top-right-bottom-left

These utilities apply to the `inset` CSS property, which is a shorthand for `top`, `right`, `bottom`, and `left`. They support numeric, fractional, pixel, full percentage, auto, custom property, and arbitrary values, including negative variants.

```css
/* inset-<number> */
inset: calc(var(--spacing) * <number>);
```

```css
/* -inset-<number> */
inset: calc(var(--spacing) * -<number>);
```

```css
/* inset-<fraction> */
inset: calc(<fraction> * 100%);
```

```css
/* -inset-<fraction> */
inset: calc(<fraction> * -100%);
```

```css
/* inset-px */
inset: 1px;
```

```css
/* -inset-px */
inset: -1px;
```

```css
/* inset-full */
inset: 100%;
```

```css
/* -inset-full */
inset: -100%;
```

```css
/* inset-auto */
inset: auto;
```

```css
/* inset-(<custom-property>) */
inset: var(<custom-property>);
```

```css
/* inset-[<value>] */
inset: <value>;
```

### Configure subpath imports in package.json

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/functions-and-directives

Define subpath imports in package.json to create path aliases for directives like @import, @reference, @plugin, and @config. These work similarly to bundler and TypeScript path aliases.

```JSON
{
  "imports": {
    "#app.css": "./src/css/app.css"
  }
}
```

```css
}
```

### Responsive transition property with breakpoint variant - HTML/Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/transition-property

Demonstrates applying transition utilities conditionally at specific breakpoints using the md: prefix. The transition-none class applies by default, then switches to transition-all at medium screen sizes and above.

```html
<button class="transition-none md:transition-all ..."><!-- ... --></button>
```

---

### Constraining Images and Videos to Parent Width with Preflight CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/preflight

This Preflight CSS rule ensures images and videos are responsive by setting `max-width: 100%` and `height: auto`. This prevents them from overflowing their containers while preserving their intrinsic aspect ratio, making them adapt to different screen sizes.

```css
img,
video {
  max-width: 100%;
  height: auto;
}
```

---

### Apply custom filter values with bracket notation

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/filter

Demonstrates using the filter-[<value>] syntax to apply completely custom filter values, such as SVG filter references. This allows for advanced filtering beyond the predefined Tailwind utilities.

```html
<img
  class="filter-[url('filters.svg#filter-id')] ..."
  src="/img/mountains.jpg"
/>
```

---

### Add Viewport Meta Tag for Responsive Design in HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

This HTML snippet demonstrates how to include the viewport meta tag in the `<head>` of a document. This tag is crucial for responsive web design as it controls the viewport's width and scaling on different devices, ensuring proper rendering of responsive layouts.

```html
<meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0" />
```

---

### Apply custom min-height values in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/min-height

Use min-h-[<value>] syntax for arbitrary custom pixel values, or min-h-(<custom-property>) syntax to reference CSS custom properties with automatic var() wrapping.

```html
<div class="min-h-[220px] ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

```html
<div class="min-h-(--my-min-height) ...">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

### Using negative order values with dash prefix

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/order

Prefix the order class name with a dash to convert it to a negative value. This allows setting negative order values for flex and grid items.

```html
<div class="-order-1">
  <!-- ... -->
</div>
```

---

### Sepia Filter with Custom Values in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/filter-sepia

Apply custom sepia filter values using bracket notation syntax sepia-[<value>] for arbitrary values, or use CSS custom properties with sepia-(<custom-property>) syntax. The custom property syntax automatically wraps the value in var() function.

```html
<img class="sepia-[.25]" src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
<img class="sepia-(--my-sepia)" src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
```

---

### Apply saturate filter using CSS custom properties

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/filter-saturate

Use the saturate-(<custom-property>) syntax as shorthand for saturate-[var(<custom-property>)]. This automatically wraps the custom property in the var() function for dynamic saturation control.

```html
<img class="saturate-(--my-saturation) ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
```

### Apply `snap-normal` for skipping scroll snap stops in HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/scroll-snap-stop

This HTML snippet illustrates the use of the `snap-normal` utility, allowing a scroll container to skip past potential snap positions without forcing a stop. It sets up a horizontal scrollable gallery where images are potential snap points but the user can smoothly scroll past them without being forced to stop at each one.

```html
<div class="snap-x ...">
  <div class="snap-center snap-normal ...">
    <img src="/img/vacation-01.jpg" />
  </div>
  <div class="snap-center snap-normal ...">
    <img src="/img/vacation-02.jpg" />
  </div>
  <div class="snap-center snap-normal ...">
    <img src="/img/vacation-03.jpg" />
  </div>
  <div class="snap-center snap-normal ...">
    <img src="/img/vacation-04.jpg" />
  </div>
  <div class="snap-center snap-normal ...">
    <img src="/img/vacation-05.jpg" />
  </div>
  <div class="snap-center snap-normal ...">
    <img src="/img/vacation-06.jpg" />
  </div>
</div>
```

Use breakpoint prefixes like `md:` with caret color utilities to apply different cursor colors at specific screen sizes. This enables responsive design patterns for caret styling.

---

### Manage Utility Class Duplication Using Templating Loops in HTML

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/styling-with-utility-classes

This HTML snippet demonstrates how to effectively manage utility class duplication by rendering elements within a templating loop (e.g., `{#each ...}`). The utility classes for the avatar image are defined only once, and the loop dynamically generates multiple instances, thereby eliminating the need for repetitive class declarations in the source markup.

```html
<div>
  <div class="flex items-center space-x-2 text-base">
    <h4 class="font-semibold text-slate-900">Contributors</h4>
    <span
      class="bg-slate-100 px-2 py-1 text-xs font-semibold text-slate-700 ..."
      >204</span
    >
  </div>
  <div class="mt-3 flex -space-x-2 overflow-hidden">
    {#each contributors as user}
    <img
      class="inline-block h-12 w-12 rounded-full ring-2 ring-white"
      src="{user.avatarUrl}"
      alt="{user.handle}"
    />
    {/each}
  </div>
  <div class="mt-3 text-sm font-medium">
    <a href="#" class="text-blue-500">+ 198 others</a>
  </div>
</div>
```

### place-content-between - Distribute with Space Between

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/place-content

Distributes grid items with equal space between them on both axes using place-content-between. Items are spaced so gaps are equal between rows and columns.

```html
<div class="grid h-48 grid-cols-2 place-content-between gap-4 ...">
  <div>01</div>
  <div>02</div>
  <div>03</div>
  <div>04</div>
</div>
```

### Space Y Arbitrary Value Margin CSS Implementation

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/margin

CSS implementation for vertical spacing with arbitrary custom values. Supports any CSS value through bracket notation with directional control.

```css
& > :not(:last-child) {
  --tw-space-y-reverse: 0;
  margin-block-start: calc(<value> * var(--tw-space-y-reverse));
  margin-block-end: calc(<value> * calc(1 - var(--tw-space-y-reverse)));
}
```

```html
<p class="text-sm/7 ...">So I started to walk into the water...</p>
<p class="text-sm/8 ...">So I started to walk into the water...</p>
```

### Tailwind CSS `translate` Utility Class Reference

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/translate

This section provides a comprehensive reference of Tailwind CSS utility classes for translating elements. Each entry maps a utility class to its generated CSS `translate` property, demonstrating how elements are moved along the x, y, and z axes using various units like spacing scale, percentages, pixels, custom properties, and arbitrary values.

```css
translate: calc(var(--spacing) * <number>) calc(var(--spacing) * <number>);
```

```css
translate: calc(var(--spacing) * -<number>) calc(var(--spacing) * -<number>);
```

```css
translate: calc(<fraction> * 100%) calc(<fraction> * 100%);
```

```css
translate: calc(<fraction> * -100%) calc(<fraction> * -100%);
```

```css
translate: 100% 100%;
```

```css
translate: -100% -100%;
```

```css
translate: 1px 1px;
```

```css
translate: -1px -1px;
```

```css
translate: var(<custom-property>) var(<custom-property>);
```

```css
translate: <value> <value>;
```

```css
translate: calc(var(--spacing) * <number>) var(--tw-translate-y);
```

```css
translate: calc(var(--spacing) * -<number>) var(--tw-translate-y);
```

```css
translate: calc(<fraction> * 100%) var(--tw-translate-y);
```

```css
translate: calc(<fraction> * -100%) var(--tw-translate-y);
```

```css
translate: 100% var(--tw-translate-y);
```

```css
translate: -100% var(--tw-translate-y);
```

```css
translate: 1px var(--tw-translate-y);
```

```css
translate: -1px var(--tw-translate-y);
```

```css
translate: var(<custom-property>) var(--tw-translate-y);
```

```css
translate: <value> var(--tw-translate-y);
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) calc(var(--spacing) * <number>);
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) calc(var(--spacing) * -<number>);
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) calc(<fraction> * 100%);
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) calc(<fraction> * -100%);
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) 100%;
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) -100%;
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) 1px;
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) -1px;
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) var(<custom-property>);
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) <value>;
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) var(--tw-translate-y)
  calc(var(--spacing) * <number>);
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) var(--tw-translate-y)
  calc(var(--spacing) * -<number>);
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) var(--tw-translate-y) 1px;
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) var(--tw-translate-y) -1px;
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) var(--tw-translate-y) var(<custom-property>);
```

```css
translate: var(--tw-translate-x) var(--tw-translate-y) <value>;
```

```css
translate: none;
```

### Control Gradient Stop Positions with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/background-image

Demonstrates how to precisely adjust the position of gradient color stops using Tailwind CSS utilities such as `from-<percentage>`, `via-<percentage>`, and `to-<percentage>`. This allows for fine-grained control over the gradient's color distribution.

```html
<div
  class="bg-gradient-to-r from-indigo-500 from-10% via-sky-500 via-30% to-emerald-500 to-90% ..."
></div>
```


```HTML
</div>
```

```HTML
<div class="inset-(--my-position) ...">
  <!-- ... -->
```

### Create Functional Custom Utility with Arguments

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/adding-custom-styles

Register functional utilities that accept arguments using the @utility directive with wildcard syntax. The --value() function resolves the utility value from Tailwind's configuration.

```css
@utility tab-* {
  tab-size: --value(--tab-size-*);
}
```

### Create Custom Color Palette from Scratch

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/colors

Completely replace the default Tailwind color palette by disabling all colors with --color-\*: initial and defining a custom set of colors.

```css
@import "tailwindcss";
@theme {
  --color-*: initial;
  --color-white: #fff;
  --color-purple: #3f3cbb;
  --color-midnight: #121063;
  --color-tahiti: #3ab7bf;
  --color-bermuda: #78dcca;
}
```

### Apply logical padding with Tailwind CSS `ps/pe-<number>` utilities for LTR/RTL

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/padding

Explains how to use `ps-<number>` (padding-inline-start) and `pe-<number>` (padding-inline-end) utilities. These logical properties adjust padding based on text direction (LTR or RTL), providing flexible internationalization support.

```html
<div>
  <div dir="ltr">
    <div class="ps-8 ...">ps-8</div>
    <div class="pe-8 ...">pe-8</div>
  </div>
  <div dir="rtl">
    <div class="ps-8 ...">ps-8</div>
    <div class="pe-8 ...">pe-8</div>
  </div>
</div>
```

### Space X Reverse Direction CSS Implementation

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/margin

CSS implementation for reversing horizontal spacing direction. Sets --tw-space-x-reverse to 1 to flip spacing to the opposite side of child elements.

```css
& > :not(:last-child) {
  --tw-space-x-reverse: 1;
}
```

### Float using logical properties with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/float

Use the float-start and float-end utility classes to float elements using logical properties that automatically map to left or right based on text direction (LTR or RTL). This enables proper internationalization support.

```html
<article>
  <img class="float-start ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
  <p>Maybe we can live without libraries, people like you and me. ...</p>
</article>
<article dir="rtl">
  <img class="float-start ..." src="/img/mountains.jpg" />
  <p>... ربما يمكننا العيش بدون مكتبات، أشخاص مثلي ومثلك. ربما. بالتأكيد</p>
</article>
```

### Load legacy JavaScript config with @config directive (CSS)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/functions-and-directives

The `@config` directive allows loading a legacy JavaScript-based configuration file within your CSS. This enables incremental migration by merging CSS-defined configurations with existing JavaScript ones, with CSS taking precedence. Note that `corePlugins`, `safelist`, and `separator` options from the JavaScript config are not supported in v4.0.

```css
@config "../../tailwind.config.js";
```

### Space Y Custom Property Margin CSS Implementation

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/margin

CSS implementation for vertical spacing using custom CSS properties. Allows dynamic spacing values through CSS variables with calc() for directional computation.

```css
& > :not(:last-child) {
  --tw-space-y-reverse: 0;
  margin-block-start: calc(var(<custom-property>) * var(--tw-space-y-reverse));
  margin-block-end: calc(
    var(<custom-property>) * calc(1 - var(--tw-space-y-reverse))
  );
}
```

### Custom grid-row values with arbitrary values in Tailwind CSS

### Apply backdrop sepia filter with Tailwind CSS utilities

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/backdrop-filter-sepia

Use backdrop-sepia utility classes to apply sepia effects to an element's backdrop. Supports predefined intensity levels (0-100), custom values via bracket notation, and CSS variables. Can be combined with responsive breakpoint variants like md: for conditional application.

```html
<div class="bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)]">
  <div class="bg-white/30 backdrop-sepia-0 ..."></div>
</div>
<div class="bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)]">
  <div class="bg-white/30 backdrop-sepia-50 ..."></div>
</div>
<div class="bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)]">
  <div class="bg-white/30 backdrop-sepia ..."></div>
</div>
```

```html
<div class="flex flex-col md:flex-row ..."><!-- ... --></div>
```

---

### Tailwind CSS Inset Ring Color Variable Definitions (System & Palettes)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/box-shadow

This snippet presents the CSS custom property definitions for Tailwind CSS's `inset-ring` color utilities. It defines the `--tw-inset-ring-color` variable, supporting system-defined colors like `inherit`, `currentColor`, `transparent`, `black`, and `white`, as well as specific color palettes such as red and orange. Each definition maps a utility class to its corresponding CSS variable and color value, often with an OKLCH comment.

```css
--tw-inset-ring-color: inherit;
--tw-inset-ring-color: currentColor;
--tw-inset-ring-color: transparent;
--tw-inset-ring-color: var(--color-black); /* #000 */
--tw-inset-ring-color: var(--color-white); /* #fff */
--tw-inset-ring-color: var(--color-red-50); /* oklch(97.1% 0.013 17.38) */
--tw-inset-ring-color: var(--color-red-100); /* oklch(93.6% 0.032 17.717) */
--tw-inset-ring-color: var(--color-red-200); /* oklch(88.5% 0.062 18.334) */
```

### Position Elements with Top, Right, Bottom, Left Utilities in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/top-right-bottom-left

Demonstrates basic positioning using Tailwind CSS utilities to pin elements to corners, span edges, and fill parent containers. Uses absolute positioning with top-0, right-0, bottom-0, left-0, and inset utilities to achieve various layout patterns.

```HTML
<!-- Pin to top left corner -->
<div class="relative size-32 ...">
  <div class="absolute top-0 left-0 size-16 ...">01</div>
</div>
<!-- Span top edge -->
<div class="relative size-32 ...">
  <div class="absolute inset-x-0 top-0 h-16 ...">02</div>
</div>
<!-- Pin to top right corner -->
<div class="relative size-32 ...">
  <div class="absolute top-0 right-0 size-16 ...">03</div>
</div>
<!-- Span left edge -->
<div class="relative size-32 ...">
  <div class="absolute inset-y-0 left-0 w-16 ...">04</div>
</div>
<!-- Fill entire parent -->
<div class="relative size-32 ...">
  <div class="absolute inset-0 ...">05</div>
</div>
<!-- Span right edge -->
<div class="relative size-32 ...">
  <div class="absolute inset-y-0 right-0 w-16 ...">06</div>
</div>
<!-- Pin to bottom left corner -->
<div class="relative size-32 ...">
  <div class="absolute bottom-0 left-0 size-16 ...">07</div>
</div>
<!-- Span bottom edge -->
<div class="relative size-32 ...">
  <div class="absolute inset-x-0 bottom-0 h-16 ...">08</div>
</div>
<!-- Pin to bottom right corner -->
<div class="relative size-32 ...">
  <div class="absolute right-0 bottom-0 size-16 ...">09</div>
</div>
```

### Creating arbitrary Tailwind CSS `group-*` variants with custom selectors

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This section demonstrates the flexibility of creating custom `group-*` variants using arbitrary values. It allows developers to define specific selectors (e.g., `group-[.is-published]:block`) to apply styles, and also shows how to use the `&` character for precise control over selector placement in the generated CSS.

```html
<div class="group is-published">
  <div class="hidden group-[.is-published]:block">Published</div>
</div>
```

```html
<div class="group">
  <div class="group-[:nth-of-type(3)_&]:block"><!-- ... --></div>
</div>
```

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/box-shadow

This snippet details the CSS custom property definitions for Tailwind CSS's `ring-{color}` utilities, specifically for the neutral and stone color palettes. Each line maps a utility class to the `--tw-ring-color` variable, assigning it a value from a predefined color variable (e.g., `--color-neutral-100`) along with its OKLCH representation in a comment. --tw-ring-color: var(--color-stone-100); /* oklch(97% 0.001 106.424) */
```css
--tw-ring-color: var(--color-stone-200); /* oklch(92.3% 0.003 48.717) */
--tw-ring-color: var(--color-stone-300); /* oklch(86.9% 0.005 56.366) */
--tw-ring-color: var(--color-stone-400); /* oklch(70.9% 0.01 56.259) */
--tw-ring-color: var(--color-stone-500); /* oklch(55.3% 0.013 58.071) */
--tw-ring-color: var(--color-stone-600); /* oklch(44.4% 0.011 73.639) */
```

```html
    <div>RAM</div>
    <a href="#"> See performance specs </a>
  </div>

    class="mt-4 grid grid-cols-6 gap-2 pointer-coarse:mt-6 pointer-coarse:grid-cols-3 pointer-coarse:gap-4"
  >
    <label class="p-2 pointer-coarse:p-4 ...">
      <input
        type="radio"
        name="memory-option"

        className="sr-only"
      />
      <span>4 GB</span>
    </label>

```

### Using Underscores for Spaces in Tailwind CSS Arbitrary Variants

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/hover-focus-and-other-states

This snippet demonstrates how to include spaces within an arbitrary variant's selector by using underscores (`_`). This allows for targeting descendant elements (e.g., `[&_p]` selects all `<p>` elements within the current element) directly in your HTML classes, mimicking CSS descendant selectors.

```html
<div class="[&_p]:mt-4">
  <p>Lorem ipsum...</p>
  <ul>
    <li><p>Lorem ipsum...</p></li>
    <!-- ... -->
  </ul>
</div>
```

```html
  class="border-separate border-spacing-2 border border-gray-400 dark:border-gray-500"
>

      <th class="border border-gray-300 dark:border-gray-600">City</th>
    </tr>

      <td class="border border-gray-300 dark:border-gray-700">Indianapolis</td>
    </tr>

    </tr>

    </tr>

</table>
```

---

### Apply Start-Start Border Radius in Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/border-radius

Applies border-radius to the start-start corner (top-left in LTR, top-right in RTL) using rounded-ss-\* utility classes. Supports predefined scales (xs through 4xl), none, full, custom properties, and arbitrary values. Enables logical directional styling for internationalization.

```css
/* rounded-ss-xs */
border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-xs); /* 0.125rem (2px) */

/* rounded-ss-sm */
border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-sm); /* 0.25rem (4px) */

/* rounded-ss-md */
border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-md); /* 0.375rem (6px) */

/* rounded-ss-lg */
border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-lg); /* 0.5rem (8px) */

/* rounded-ss-xl */
border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-xl); /* 0.75rem (12px) */

/* rounded-ss-2xl */
border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-2xl); /* 1rem (16px) */

/* rounded-ss-3xl */
border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-3xl); /* 1.5rem (24px) */

/* rounded-ss-4xl */
border-start-start-radius: var(--radius-4xl); /* 2rem (32px) */

/* rounded-ss-none */
border-start-start-radius: 0;

/* rounded-ss-full */
border-start-start-radius: calc(infinity * 1px);

/* rounded-ss-[<value>] */
border-start-start-radius: <value>;
```

### Apply Inset Ring Colors with CSS Variables

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/box-shadow

Tailwind CSS inset ring color utilities that set the --tw-inset-ring-color CSS variable with color palette values. Supports multiple color families (gray, zinc, neutral, stone) with intensity levels from 50 to 950, each mapped to OKLCH color space values for consistent color rendering.

```css
--tw-inset-ring-color: var(--color-gray-900); /* oklch(21% 0.034 264.665) */
--tw-inset-ring-color: var(--color-zinc-500); /* oklch(55.2% 0.016 285.938) */
--tw-inset-ring-color: var(--color-neutral-600); /* oklch(43.9% 0 0) */
--tw-inset-ring-color: var(--color-stone-700); /* oklch(37.4% 0.01 67.558) */
```

### Correctly Apply Mobile-First Text Alignment with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/responsive-design

This HTML snippet demonstrates the correct mobile-first approach for text alignment in Tailwind CSS. By applying `text-center` as an unprefixed utility, text is centered on mobile screens by default. Then, `sm:text-left` overrides this behavior to left-align text on screens 640px and wider, adhering to Tailwind's mobile-first philosophy.

```html
<!-- This will center text on mobile, and left align it on screens 640px and wider -->
<div class="text-center sm:text-left"></div>
```

### Apply wrap-anywhere class for flexible text wrapping in flex containers

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/overflow-wrap

The wrap-anywhere utility applies overflow-wrap: anywhere and allows the browser to factor mid-word line breaks when calculating element intrinsic size. Particularly useful in flex containers where child elements need to shrink below content size without setting min-width: 0.

```html

  <img class="size-16 rounded-full" src="/img/profile.jpg" />

    <p>jason.riemenschneider@vandelayindustries.com</p>
  </div>
</div>
```

### Apply Dynamic Styles in React with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/styling-with-utility-classes

This React component demonstrates how to use inline `style` attributes to apply dynamic `backgroundColor` and `color` values, which are passed as props. This approach is ideal when style values originate from dynamic sources like databases or APIs, while still utilizing Tailwind's utility classes for other styling properties.

```jsx
export function BrandedButton({ buttonColor, textColor, children }) {
  return (
    <button
      style={{
        backgroundColor: buttonColor,
        color: textColor,
      }}
      className="rounded-md px-3 py-1.5 font-medium"
    >
      {children}
    </button>
  );
}
```

### Define Utility Values from Tailwind CSS Theme Keys

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/adding-custom-styles

This snippet demonstrates how to use the `--value(--theme-key-*)` syntax within an `@utility` directive to resolve utility values against predefined theme keys in Tailwind CSS. This enables the generation of dynamic utilities like `tab-2` or `tab-github` based on theme configurations.

```css
@theme {
  --tab-size-2: 2;
  --tab-size-4: 4;
  --tab-size-github: 8;
}
@utility tab-* {
  tab-size: --value(--tab-size-*);
}
```

### Apply mask-composite utilities in HTML with Tailwind CSS

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/mask-composite

This snippet demonstrates how to apply various `mask-composite` utilities (`mask-add`, `mask-subtract`, `mask-intersect`, `mask-exclude`) directly within HTML using Tailwind CSS classes. It shows how to combine multiple mask images and positions with a background image to achieve different masking effects.

```html
<div
  class="mask-add mask-[url(/img/circle.png),url(/img/circle.png)] mask-[position:30%_50%,70%_50%] bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)]"
></div>
<div
  class="mask-subtract mask-[url(/img/circle.png),url(/img/circle.png)] mask-[position:30%_50%,70%_50%] bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)]"
></div>
<div
  class="mask-intersect mask-[url(/img/circle.png),url(/img/circle.png)] mask-[position:30%_50%,70%_50%] bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)]"
></div>
<div
  class="mask-exclude mask-[url(/img/circle.png),url(/img/circle.png)] mask-[position:30%_50%,70%_50%] bg-[url(/img/mountains.jpg)]"
></div>
```

### Custom CSS Button Component with Tailwind Theme Variables

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/styling-with-utility-classes

Custom CSS class using Tailwind's @layer directive and theme variables to create a reusable button component. Demonstrates how to define custom CSS for simple components when template partials feel excessive, maintaining design consistency through CSS variables.

```html
<button class="btn-primary">Save changes</button>
```

```css
@import "tailwindcss";

@layer components {
  .btn-primary {
    border-radius: calc(infinity * 1px);
    background-color: var(--color-violet-500);
    padding-inline: --spacing(5);
    padding-block: --spacing(2);
    font-weight: var(--font-weight-semibold);
    color: var(--color-white);
    box-shadow: var(--shadow-md);
    &:hover {
      @media (hover: hover) {
        background-color: var(--color-violet-700);
      }
    }
  }
}
```

### Reference Other Variables in Color Definitions

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/colors

Use @theme inline to define colors that reference other CSS variables, enabling theme-aware color switching across different data attributes or media queries.

```css
@import "tailwindcss";
:root {
  --acme-canvas-color: oklch(0.967 0.003 264.542);
}
[data-theme="dark"] {
  --acme-canvas-color: oklch(0.21 0.034 264.665);
}
@theme inline {
  --color-canvas: var(--acme-canvas-color);
}
```

### Reduced Motion Support with Motion-Safe Variant

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/animation

Demonstrates using the `motion-safe:` variant to conditionally apply animations only when the user has not specified a preference for reduced motion. This ensures accessibility for users with motion sensitivity.

```html
<button type="button" class="bg-indigo-600 ..." disabled>
  <svg class="mr-3 size-5 motion-safe:animate-spin ..." viewBox="0 0 24 24">
    <!-- ... -->
  </svg>
  Processing
</button>
```

---

### Load legacy JavaScript plugin with @plugin directive (CSS)

Source: https://tailwindcss.com/docs/functions-and-directives

The `@plugin` directive is used to load legacy JavaScript-based plugins directly from your CSS. It accepts either a package name for published plugins or a local file path for custom plugins, allowing for continued use of v3.x plugins during migration.

```css
@plugin "@tailwindcss/typography";
```
